In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body that one can feel it, administer extraction with tweezers; and it is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, then you treat them with subtle tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the cannula of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed in forming all the chain; do this so often that all the worms come out.  And if they do not obey to come out, then stuff around the chain with cotton as I have said about the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have experienced in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and your medicines into the ear to all this instrument, for this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be of silver or brass narrow below at i. small openings, and above open for distilling; and for pressing inside the distillation i. instrument of brass well made for this, and if you see take i. razor and wrap around the point evenly cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the chain, and the chain be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be i. pock heated over a fire then one distils it into the ear; and keep that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through the closing of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these closures come at times from within the ear, if one cannot see them; and at times it comes .i. pock of pus, and one sees well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes from within, if one cannot see it, is of great healing in more dispositions, and in this one sees that you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opening, then the work has all these spatulation, as to what this one is formed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it sharp and trenches in front and behind all plain, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opening is of flesh born or core of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, as long as that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the impaction is in the ear, take one razor fine and light, and heat it a little in the fire, then put it in the body of the ear. If you feel the impaction which the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce gently, and guard that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerate which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, dip a sponge and drape it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are or treated by distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper of the sheets
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This healing that comes on paper of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, so you should extend them with tweezers and pliers, and cut from a spatula at their roots; then put over it powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decorticate, so you cauterize with the subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is worth moving; and many times repair, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, so are those roots burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gristle
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times in papers come to the eyes things that seem like gravel in its shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstorm," and is an assembly of moisture thick in the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the hailstorm moves from one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the large opening, then the skin of each part lightly, then take pliers, and cut. If you cannot cut without perceiving a hole in the paper, then it does not harm the patient; and if the fissure is great, so assemble it with a suture, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, because the eye returns it quickly and forms flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstorm is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over, and being the hailstorm with pliers, and cut it and press on one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by incision, it does not harm; and when the hailstorm is cut, let the eye water with salt water, and cure the place of that which forms flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	This is an eye grease that is made in the webs of papers above, and this happens more to children than to others, and grieves much their eyes, and they come to them the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun for that the tears hasten to their eyes; and for that they lie down they on their faces aside, and sleep upon it, and are their papers below their eyebrows moist that the inflammation and the appearance have covered with the exinach which opens in the eye. And when you press its place with your fingers and feel the exirnach between.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in your bosom; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach of each part, then put it on top of it; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture on the spatumile a notch of a width, and not be more than large as the wound that you make to the vein; and make the skin in part until you come to the exinach; and in more arrangements comes exinach from the opening, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract therefore a whole piece of cloth charpit between your fingers at the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the opening, that you do not come to all the spatumile up to the eye, that you do not blind it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the crack, then slightly enlarge the crack until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten bandages in wine and water, and put them on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if to such men who grind flaxseed and put it on in order to corrupt the moisture which has stagnated. Then cure it until it is healed. And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then cure it with ointments soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on paper the hairs grow adjusted other than nature's, and are old, they harm the eyes, and bring manner of maladies like tears accustomed, and softenings of the papers and albugine, as much as it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery altogether fire, or by medicine ague according to what it is before or chapter of cautery, and is done or by incision and stitch or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the chief of the patient on your healthy, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if that no, there puts an needle to all .i. thread above; and be that below the margin of the paper or the hair grows beside those hairs, and draws .i. thread to the above to all the paper, and turns it to the razor; then does in the part below the paper, below the hairs adjusted, to all the spatula cutting, from the great tear to the small; then extracts .i. thread, and puts below the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then seizes on the paper a figure of ench, like the leaf of myrtle, and altogether it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is who has need that one copes a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened; then does on all the spatula above the .ij. lines that you have signed, and commences from the lou grant tear to the small; and be it one of the clefts near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then puts the oncine in one of the .ij. angles of the heart, then scrapes it all; then assembles the .ij. lips to a stitch of an needle to all .i. thread of fine wool, and wipes the blood, and does make aird the superfluity of the threads above the .ij. eyebrows to any sticky things, if you see to do this; and if not, then has no care, then leaves the stitch and the threads up to .iij. days or .iiij.; then cures the wound without stitch of drying and constricting things, because the paper revives at the joining of the wound and the assembling of it, but the stitch is moved (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another manner: and it is that you trace the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, at three ounces severed according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle which has one thread, and put it in the figure; and put another thread beside the big tear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then raise your hand equally, and raise all the skin over what you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper is converted: so it behooves you to use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the wounds is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the fold inside according to what I have said, and then make .ij. canes by art, and .ij. subtle liens as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut off the .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above what surmounts the paper of the eye, and strain the .ij. canes of the .ij. parts form; and let it stay thus for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and rise, until it heals by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with more force, and then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is soldered, and if it has been lifted the paper, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the .ij. canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you prick an agile needle, and it puts .i. thread of silk soft and subtle; then assemble the shoulders and tie one and the other subtly, and be the length of the threads a palm long; then order in the chase another fine thread of silk briefly, and tie the chief of the thread; then put the patient's head on your healthy; and be below the sun so that the works are declared, because it is one work subtle and small, then put the needle to all the chase in the root of the hair adjusted, and make it pierce in the paper carefully until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there is .i. or .ij. or .iij. or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, so you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the hole above and that you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for .ij. days or .iij., until the hair hardens in its place and grows the flesh above; and if the hairs are small, so accompany one long hair from the natural hooves, and be raised with that one or you leave it, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this sickness which is called "aleacrati" or the rot comes to the eye, it comes in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens through sudden wound, or incision or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of operation on it is that you cut open that suture and separate its lips, and put inside a tent of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it does not behoove you to use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain. Because if you do this, the disease returns worse than the first; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the rose of water or aloe and linseed seeds are cooked, and diaquilon ointment melted in any of the oils, and a tent is wrapped around it, and it cures with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form it was before; and these operations that we have said are nothing but addresses for this illness, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the char which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This sickness that is desoz which truly is called «axacrati», and is natural and accidental. The accidents come from wound and fissure and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you prick an needle, in which it has .i. double thread, and put it into the char, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the threads comes into .ij. chiefs of the char; then is the char above all the needle, and the cut is at .i. spatumile wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it ought, it is good; if not, then take .i. razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make .ij. fissures or cuts inside the paper; and let the chiefs of the .ij. fissures be at the .ij. angles of the incision that you have cut, and make angles so that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no «.j. griesche»; then remove that char, according to the quantity that its edges are gone under, from those that follow the paper, then join the .ij. parts together, and stitch them with a thread of linen; then cure it with what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a split or seam or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain split under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the ailment, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip anything of all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what it is necessary of work and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper's  humidity
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering occurs to the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is soldered with the white of the egg, and cannot move or do its natural work, then it is necessary that you put the tip of a razor under the paper, and raise it up; and the extent as pinches, as long as you cut what is hard to the spatula subtly, which is not too thick nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer that the spatula is too thick or bleaches the eye; and let your incision, with which you scrape that assembly, be slightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it is healed all that assembly, and make no times in the salt water of the eye, and the sweet water lift, and coliere; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in an abundance of egg; and after the third day use the coliere and the things sudans as long as it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in two ways: it is fleshy and seeming to one hard skin, and another which is not fleshy, but seems like white frozen moisture, that when one touches it with iron and one cures it by pincers, one cannot; and the one and the other semblance begins towards the great tear, and crosses point by point until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then he opens his eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coils the angle with small pliers, and the one above; then take a needle, and put it one hair of horse, or deer, or ox, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a point and stick it in the angle, and pierce it to the whole needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the one above, and scrape to all the hair the side of the angle which follows the eyebrow and the silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear to the whole spatula subtly and with small forces, and leave the natural flesh or tear, so that by incision does not come the body of tears accustomed; and at no time is the angle placed only once, and to the thread, as we have said; then scrape it all over the spatula from this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the spatula does not touch the fleshy veil and break it, and that the prickle is not pierced; and after the incision throw into the eye a little bit of silk ground up, and from the collar made of litharge, and let it remain until the next day; then cure it as it requires until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved, and you cannot push the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, so work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula lighter point according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail subtly, and if you see that it diminishes not and the reason is hastened, then distill from your mouth into the eye collar made of litharge and red collar and silk ground up, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same operation, as long as it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a boil, then cauterize, and cure the boil first until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it with a bandage, and cut a part and not half, that body of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of lead white.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which is born on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men are born at times with red flesh, and it covers the iris and restrains upon the eyelids, and turns them outward, and it seems like a rose of bolster; and the work is that the patient puts his head into your healthy one, then operates the eyes, and coils all that flesh with bandages suitable to this, and supports it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting all the way down to the end, and be careful that you do not blind the eye during the operation; and let the incision of the spathule be as we have said in the incision of the angle and with little forces from which one removes the sebacle, as how it is formed after this chapter he demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then apply the oil of silphium or you distill red mercury and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top of the eye cotton with egg white, so that it may be assured of a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the pus does not rise to the surface, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as long as flesh is adjusted in the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it is necessary that you align the cure of each weak eye of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in surgery of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from the work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Veins are red and covered over the eye, and they take away from sight their work and weaken the eye all days. It is necessary therefore that first you look at the eye, in what way it is, if it is before, and there is no other disease except for the vein; therefore the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your shoulder, then suspend those veins at all the circumference according to his wisdom, and let the circumference be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two circumferences be by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then this coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe away the blood hour after another, until you see remove those veins from the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatula, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill into the eye  green and red colic for to corrupt what is remaining of the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to gather all these in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things that appease the pain of the eyes, and let it rest for several days until the pain is appeased and the abscess is assured hot, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and medicine burning according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it should die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see corruption and blackness, then the king has all the instruments of what here are the form; and it is called “sharp chief,” and is made of fire iron to one chief point, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it upon the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little as long as you know that this corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the parts are joined, and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is joined, and remains so for forty days, and it does not renew or become inflamed, and no bad accident comes to it, know that it is cured; if this is not the case, then there is no other way but to bring the fistula back to the opening according to this form: and that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take one piece according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and the shaft be thinned until the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone next to the lacrimal, and move your hand from the eye i.e. 1 finger's width, then turn all of the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he holds his hand on his cheek; and then return the place of dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the ligaments, then it goes to the cheek; thus it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no disturbance to the cheek or decrease, it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal, then place suction cups or a haterel without injuring to suck, then put on the eye i.i. linen made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and place it over bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths enough soft, and double each in .iiij., and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye has need; then strain by means of a firm bandage above, and recommence the suction cups to suck without injuring; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the linen softens, it is necessary that you strain it tightly; then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good; if not; then recommence the application and cloths and linen and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the displacement of woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then open it, and there comes forth some papers as .i. grains of resins, and it is esperantauble to see; therefore if you saw it covered, the work is such that you put an awl in the root of the lower part until that of above, then put another awl where there is .i. double thread of the edge of the lamier; and let it pierce, and leave the first awl according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then extract the awl and put on the oiled linen half in a basin of egg; and leave it until the threads fall with the grape, then cure the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the grape each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show a great appearance, then pierce them with a subtle spatula which comes from the oil, and correct the albuminous moisture and descend the eyes, and enter in this way; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye's cavity
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the cavity of the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit upon one seat properly arranged and straight, then take the head between your hands on two parts, and move it until you see the cavity coming upwards to your eyes; then be so as to fix it, and do not descend and be disordered the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend downwards, know that it is water, and if the descent of the cavity is not properly arranged as we have said. So make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make upon the cornea one point by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the cavity issues; and when it is issued, so distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fennel is boiled and honey, then be cured of another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eyes' waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have seen the appearances of the eyes in division, and what is needed to examine them; so in work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie their healthy eye and hold it very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if their eyes are left, or in your right hand if their eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if their eyes are left, the instrument that is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if their eyes are right; then put the point of the instrument next to the cornea through the width of a rat's tail in the white part of the eye to the part closest to the tear duct, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel that the almagda comes to the hollow place; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the end of the measure of the space which is from the iris to the end of the black pupil; and this is the cornea of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then put the instrument up to where the liquid is, then squeeze it out one vein after another. If the liquid is now coming out, then the patient sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After rest i.e., a little, and if the eye goes up the second vein, put the force with the instrument, and when it is ensconced and it does not go up, gently withdraw almagda by rotating your hand a little; and then put back into the eye a drop of gold-colored oil, and leave that in the eye. Then put outside the eye a stopper or a piece of linen moistened in rose oil and in yolk of egg, and tie with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, put on top as a compress with yolk of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you prick the instrument that is called "alberit," from which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctiva and do not go too deep, but make .i. it subtle, then put in the almond as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with .i. ointment beforehand, in which he sleeps on his back in .i. dark place; and be devoid of all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not proper that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you bind this, because the water ascends hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And when the abscess comes, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and the address of this who soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed, then untie the sight and put on his face .i. orilliet to cover any day, and be in that dark house. And then goes out of the house little by little, and converts itself into its cases; and know that none of disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almond piercing, so that one sucks the water, but nonetheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of the almond, for those who do not know them they see; and be of grain properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of these be of the same subtlety, and the last in three angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the knee
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes knees are born with various  joined cartilages, because of which some seem like scorpions with many parts. And if there is such a one and it has cartilage  encrusted in a dark color, and if it has cartilage soft in good color. In that one, therefore, of those cartilages which is soft, and not encrusted, you must make the patient sit between your hands opposite the sun; and open his nostrils, and cast the oncine to those cartilages, and draw them out; then cut what you can sustain with the sharp subtle spatula from one part, as long as you know that the cartilage is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains which one cannot cover, it opens everything, i.e., with instruments subtle and light, so that nothing remains; and if without a tear or abscess is sewn, or the secort as it is necessary; and if it are malignant abscesses, then haste and cauterize them until the blood is extinguished and all the pus is removed, then put on a clean cloth and water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose works and moisture comes until the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so that instruments cannot come to cut; therefore it is necessary that you put .i. a thread of linen about a finger thick, and be knotted by the hands our, and have between each knot an inch or less; and place the patient's shoulder on the thread in its nostril at its power, and pull out smelling until it comes out through the nostril inside the mouth; and many times do children so in school, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel them one after the other so that they are as ours which are or thread. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the threads, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nostril as before; do this .iij. days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the nostril a patch of felt for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, which one distills the oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a candlestick, and conduct it thus; and if you see fit, make a closed candlestick, and let the instruments be full to cleanse the head; and have .i. handle at the top for holding when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone onto the hip
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a sickness called "telul" is born at the joint of the hip, and it grows and becomes very large until it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason you should cut it at the beginning, and all bone must be removed, then put on its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays in cutting it until it is large, he takes warning if it is hard, of dull color, of poor feeling: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts it any time, it brings great evil to the sick person; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dull color, and you see that one can cut it all, then empty the sick person and cut it without fear, and cure the place with things drying and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the hip is cut and sewed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these working cartilages, it does little good, because in some men. Therefore, when this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then adjust the two lips to one stitch, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, then you must scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips to one stitch, and restrain them, and powder on powder of dragon's blood, and incense ground; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster of strong or other plasters that bind, and let it stay until it dries by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the stitch is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men's mouths often happen within the lips abscesses hard, seeming like grains of mustard, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut above each pustule, and take with tweezers and chop in each part; then apply to the place after incision of powdered vitriol, until the blood be stanched; and then the ointment of honey, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh grows on the gums, that the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and leave to clot the wound or blood; then put on the place powdered vitriol, or other powders astringent and drying; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which happens often, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are smelly; so it is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your hands, and his chin be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do of the blackness and the greening, and the jaundice and other spots, until they are cleansed; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those no, so it starts again to re-remove the second day and the third, until you have all removed; and know that the teeth need different forms of instruments for removal, according to what the work shows them, because the scraper used to remove outside teeth have other forms than those used between teeth; and these forms and others be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you wait for the drawing as much as you can, because one must not do it badly; because it is a substance very high until then one has no excuse to remove.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to endure the ordeal, it behooves you to be certain of the tooth aching. Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks that it is the good tooth, and pulls out the healthy tooth; and all the while does not depart the pain because of this, as long as the evil remains, for we have already seen this happen to these sinners; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it behooves you to scrape around the tooth on all sides with a spatula sharp and strong to ward off the gum from all sides; then move it with your two hands or pliers subtle at the first point and point, as long as it is well loosened, then firmly affirm the pliers; and let the head of the patient in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After the tooth is pulled straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out freely, then take one of these instruments and push it gently into each side, and move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced and broken, then it behooves you to fill it with wool, where the holes are; and if you strain it subtly with pliers so that it does not break when extracting it; and it behooves you wisely to work around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And therefore well guard yourself that you do not break it, and remain a part, and return to the patient through the malice of the root greater pains than the first. And guard yourself that you do not act like ignorant healers, who by their haste and by their boldness sometimes break the jawbone, and bring not about what we have recounted; but they bring about sometimes through this great illness for the roots that remain there, or for the jawbone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or water and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, then apply vitriol powder to the spot; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to which one must use teeth first, be at long points and thick handles, that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be of well-made iron, and be toothed for gripping firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the pulling, then it is necessary that you put on top of it a cotton ball moistened in butter, for one or two days, until the place becomes soft, then insert tongs which are called "algefri", so that the head seems like a beak of a bird; and be inside made also as a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, because of this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with this, it is good; if it does not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two teeth, of which is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front in the direction of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like a large pair of pliers, whose shape is here:
