Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find for themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others and if one does not break the bone or other bones, or it can, then search for the instruments that are needed, that I have told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suitable to this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural body, and the shape is ugly, and even in virgin women, then it behooves you to know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file it or file it; therefore the rake; and if it is attached with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to .i. small beak, and let it be of sharp iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping bit by bit in hands for a few days because of the hardness of the tooth, and for those you do not move others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then the file of a piece like this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles; and in filing the tooth bit by bit over a few days gently, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plane at the end without any ridge, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then it is necessary to file the roughness until it is equal, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front moves or by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that it will move, but that it will not fall out, and you have cured them with constricting medicines, and this does not work; then it is necessary to restrain it with a thread of gold, because the silver thread becomes green and rotted, but gold never changes; and be the thread neither too large nor too small, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth are being pushed together, then take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the chips between the bad teeth, if there is one or more, until you come cleverly to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the covering up to the place where you began, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move at all; and be your ligature at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut off the threads of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and put them back between the healthy teeth, and put it in such a way that it will not touch the tongue; and then leave it as tight as possible, and if it comes undone, or the thread breaks, then restrain it with another thread; and so remain and serve thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then one puts it back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and suffering, and at any time one makes the shape of a tooth from the bone of a calf, and one puts it in the place where the lack is, and one restrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	At no time is this bond which comes from under the tongue or nature that one is born thus; or by accident of a wound sutured; and the works are such that you work the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your healthy hand, and raise the tongue; then cut the nervous bond of the large, until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from the suture of a wound, then put the probe and cut the bond of the large one; and guard that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is below; and when you have done, raise the level with rose water and assil, or cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen; and apply it to the sick person each night, so that the bond cannot become sutured. And if bleeding occurs, put on top vitriol ground; and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of fiery color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, then place the probe, and make it with a subtle spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the blood does not stop at your work, put on top vitriol ground until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then raise the level of assil and seil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes comes from inside the throat bulges which are called «godath», and they call them properly the .ij. almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and of fusse color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the decorrement of blood; but let it until it is dead, and then you will part it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of blainche color reont, and the root is subtle, have appeared the instrument to cover, but first look if the abscess chalz rests and is appeased. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his hips be in your health, and work the mouth and the preigne the serjans between his hands, and press the tongue below all the instrument, from this is the form; and be of silver or of arain subtle as well as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the oncine and stick it in the almond, and drive it upward more than you can; and do nothing of the cloths with, then cut with the instrument, from this is the form, that seems a forces; and anyway the chief are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron inde or d’andainne:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cut it with pliers, from this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be trenching on one side, and on the other part name; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and ease, and if there is a discharge of blood, gargle the patient with water, or grated pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then treat it until it is healed; and at no time when other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them like the two almonds always.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I medicated a woman of an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say one abscess of small size; and I had well closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not expire through the passage which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained so one or two days. And the abscess was to me so mounted that it had been placed two fingers by the two openings of birth. I therefore, at once, and put in one a needle, then the thread pulled out, and in the pulled out a great portion of pus; then I refixed another part in the other opening of birth, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after I put the needle into these abscesses, and cut a part, and there came out only a little bit of blood; and thus was unblocked the passage of the throat of the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I engaged it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus remained without growing; and I left these parts, and know only that God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the grapes are ripe and long, they are called "perpendicular"; and if they are soft and round, they are called "grapes." When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pustule of the abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one that is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a fusse color or black, then it is necessary that you escape the incision of it. Because there is great peril to the patient. It is therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and of its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention before; then put the needle into the grape, and pull it down, and cut it at one out of two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves the voice, and to the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of cutting, then it is necessary that you use him of a certain thing to the cauterization of the sense of fear.  And the manner of the cautery is sharp and acute. And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue with the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confis with sharp live coal, so that it is not too thick nor too light; and using the tip of this instrument, from which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him have his head a hair or one puts the medicine in it, as the men of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscles run from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the back; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it curdle and the bites of the medicine be appeased; and if you see, take cotton and surround it with any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the cane above, until the cotton hardens on the grape; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and fall after four or five days. And if you have need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, then commence it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take wormwood and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or any of them in one pot, and put them therein, and let boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument shaped as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or iron, and let the one end be put into the mouth of the sick person as long as the vapor rises to the wound by the pipe, until the wound is mortified; afterward resume frequently, until the wound dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and make it not except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a pipe and put inside its head a shard of egg, so that the mouth of the sick person does not have too much heat; for the shard of egg does not let the vapor weigh heavily on the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether well-being.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or spine of fish, or something else, lodges in the throat; so it is therefore necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with the whole instrument, so that you may move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned into the throat, it is necessary that you make the sick person vomit as long as the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it will throw out the thing airy by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to its place, it will lodge itself, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take one instrument of plank according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come into it, nor thrust in the bone; and it is better that the patient thrusts the instrument, because he knows whether the thing is harsh; if he pushes down, or he pulls up all of the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bleeding of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No time is medicine given to the bleeding, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when those do not help, then look into the throat of the patient in the sun, then that you press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the bleeding, so treat it with all i. small pin, or as fine tweezers that are good for this. And if those don't work, then take a sheep's wool, and thrust it into the throat of the patient, then thrust or the tip of the wool i. hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient remains thirsty all day. Then take a full i. goblet of cold water, and open his mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the bleeding feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will come down without regret. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take i pot where there are burning coals, and let the bottom be covered with a piece of cloth in the middle, and in this pierce the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the stick in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes to the root; and the root will now fall, and if it does not fall, begin the fumigation again many times; and allow the patient thirst, and give him salted things and others, and do not drink water; and then there is need that it be freed by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument for treating the root is, when it can be seen, like tongs bent to enter the throat; and has the appearance of a bird's beak, and has sharpness from lime, so that when it takes hold, it cannot let go; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscesses are, according to those that memory comes afterward in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in .ij. ways, one being in its own likeness, and those who hold moisture. And the second manner is for the places where they are on the body. For the abscesses of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fleshy place are other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the boil is ripe according to its completion; and if some such that it is necessary to pierce when they are mature and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses near joints. Because when an abscess comes near a joint, and it is left until it is rotten inside, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the foundation, then pierce it also as long as it is ripe; and it is not necessary that you pierce an abscess mature without complete digestion, except for the one near the foundation, so that it does not burrow deep, and become elongated inside, and there comes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is appeased, and the fever subsides, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and the suppuration and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where it depends most from the abscess, and where it appears to open more; and be the perforation long in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these that boil, according to the member. And when an abscess is in its fleshy place, it is good that you let the perforation remain as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body of the venom will be lengthened from it, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance, the lips and the depths of it will harden. And if an abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs. And it is necessary that you bring small incisions in small abscesses, and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many fends according to the semblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the heart, and cover; when it has become as one drapel, and is mortified, it is necessary to do as with buboes: and if there are any that are fended in three angles, and if there are any that are cut like the myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the angres; and if there are any where a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no chief, as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain part of it; then plug the abscess until the next day, then do nothing from then on; do this many times in stages, until all the pus is gone. Similarly if the patient is of weak strength, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old man weakened. For sometimes the spirit trembles with the evacuation of the pus, that by chance the patient dies, and you are not responsible for it. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, bring lint or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many incisions, it is necessary that you put a pad in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have covered it inward, then you must fill it with old cotton or lint shavings without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then untie it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and a little vinegar, and moisten one drape, and place it on the bleeding site many times.  And if the bleeding persists, then bring governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book; and if it is during winter, and the skin where the abscess is is very sensitive, then you must put on pads and drapes moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the skin is fleshy, then it is necessary to put on bandages moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in cures of abscesses: or I have said how one must go before the cures of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Of sores
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the boil on top of a festering abscess and moist one, it is lighter because they are of little blood. And if any of these abscesses or chief where there is no moisture, and of these fut i. abscesses that I opened or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard, rough and white stone, and cannot break; and if we had done any, it would have been to her just as well made a wound as a stone. In other abscesses coming or chief, where they come from the chief of children and the roots of ears, the opening should be always at the most dependent place, so that it may pass better pus; and cure them as it is fitting.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come from other parts or body, and are numerous, and are joined together. And each scrofulas is properly inside its side, as the others and the abscess of the chief, as we have said; and the resemblances of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are those that are malignant who do not want to obey health. Therefore in the one you see of good disposition at the touch, and is similar to the color of the body, and mute from every side and is not harmful to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery or the conduit, and is not very deep; then it is necessary that you open it above, and scarify it on each side, and the two lips of the heart as ones, if you have need of it, as we have said in abscesses of the chief; and treat little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and let not the spatula be too wide or trenching, so that the hand does not escape, and do not look too far forward, that you do not open what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and constrain the wound; and leave it as long as the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to pus. And when the bleeding has been restrained, return to your work, until you have accomplished it; then carefully check with your index finger if there remain any small pimples, cut them and cauterize them. And if in the root of the pimple there is a large vein, it is not necessary that you cut that pimple at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and leave it to hang by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole pimple, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then when there is no more superfluity for the size of the pimple. It is necessary that you intend to cut the root of it, and drain out pus, and sew it as we have said. Those pimples that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears more; and pierce it as the one before mentioned, in dependence, then administer bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with an ointment promoting healing, until it is healed.
de squinance	of a swelling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who made it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called 'epiglottis' be evacuated; and do not help them by this, because all the veins and arteries of the sick are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two cheeks.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it below three or four circles, a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision of the stylet, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those vessels are such that they are suitable for the section of the epiglottis so there is no cartilage and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to all the outside, then cleave the keel as far as it comes to the channel; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel that it comes from the place that is broken, and by the absence of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a bit.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, assemble the .ij. lips of the wound of the heart, and sew entirely alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this juice until the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault belongs to the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut open the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the sickness has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they command to sew up the wound and care for it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took a knife, and stuck it in her throat, and severed part of the channels of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called by them to cure her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood which was issuing from it, and well that it had not pierced a vein nor been conducted further than the throat, and the veins were issued through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the lady that she was hoarse of voice, and returned after to her disposition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for which reason I say that in cutting the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a bruise, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two ways: natural and accidental; the natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two ways, of which one is similar to fatty tumors, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And he should be afraid, and it is not proper to work with fire except in this which is small, and the proof and searches throughout the introduction:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like our fat, and cannot to any vein, so cut it, as we cut the others, and treat all its head, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And enclose well altogether, and treat it as is proper, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are ours, which I will say all appearances;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and or it is necessary that I say all the difference which is between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is sometimes feverish and hot-bearing, as long as the boiling is not passed, and is completed the rotting; therefore rest fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new one there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains i. a pouch, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as well as a blister, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two appearances, or gross, or moist, and very colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the new [wound], that you feel and examine first with all the instrument that is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will come or chapter which is afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of the inquisition of abscesses of the new is that you prick or most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the "entromissoire", and take care in those that are jumping [out].
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, what color it has, do it as I have said of other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the introduction moisture comes, know that it is fat, so do it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side and guard the coat where it lies so that you draw it clean with the nut.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it clean, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to us many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it remains for a bit, and the wound does not grieve, then apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and tighten the wound, and put upon it soothing things, warm poultices, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what promotes flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is bleeding heavily or otherwise quickly, and you are in haste, apply a mixture of crushed vitriol, and let it lie for two or three days, until the wound dries, and calms the flow of blood; then return to covering what remains.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the instruments for inserting, and they are in three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are also three manners: large, medium, and small, for encircling abscesses or fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and are of yellow citrine, or iron, or silver, and the most useful ones are those that are yellow, and are more proven of black lead to encircle the borders of fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And they are of three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the probes are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and so there are probes which have two bends of three ways also;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And so there are probes which have three bends, and are also of three ways; and so there are probes which have two bends, and probes of a single bend only, and are of three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these things are sharp, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, which we peel the skin for; so that one does not sever the vein nor the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these introducers are the lancets put in handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And they are of three manners: large, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And one should not use them anywhere else but in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and groins, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And at times one does i.e., another instrument small, seeming to cords of fistulas, according to this form, to which one staunches blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one puts it at times in the place which heals with a cutting of veins, and arteries, and at times returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At times the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and who wants to cure them, then it behooves him to be according to this form of this line b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the mother is lying down and is softened due to her size as women are, then make two incisions above, in two similar places.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	So that one is holding onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line b to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said of sutures and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it remain until it dries up the rest and the grease, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous boils or nodules and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture ought to be cut according to this form, from the line b. until the line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care of ointment before that as long as it is healing.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a resemblance to scrofula, then treat it as we have said in incisions of scrofulas, and if the wound returns pus, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin above it is joined, many times abscesses come, and just as much happens to the vein inflamed and with an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows this about the artery, then the abscesses are long formed by it.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it in your fingers, that is to say, extraction; and when this is about the vein, then it appears red fire-like.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is below the armpits and in the groin and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It therefore behoves to avoid the iron cure, and in the one who is at the head it behooves also to avoid it, and in the one who has an inflammation of artery made from above the skin with long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the incision well, and beautifully separate the artery from the tissues, as long as it is discovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then put below it a needle, and have it pierce until the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in two leagues, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point the place which is between the two ligatures with an introducer as long as the blood that is there comes out, and let the abscess be healed.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment that causes bowing, as long as the bone stays.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure those with ointment following this, until they are healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is near the size of the vein, then it befits you to grasp with your hand that which you can of the abscess to all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then thrust the needle below where you hold it with your hand, and make it pierce through, and have 3 threads, double, so that you draw it to the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or with a line of one of two parts and two shoulders of thread
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread is not firm enough, reinsert another needle through all the thread under the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four lengths
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut the superfluity from the core and leave what is bound
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on one cloth moistened in wine and oil, then administer treatments of poultices and ointments until he is healed
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come in the nerves when they are overworked, or by too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these happen more often in the shoulders and hips and in all places where there are joints, and this is a very painful abscess, and its color seems the color of the body, and it is in many positions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when one touches it firmly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not at all like a feeling in the body, but under the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and let it stay still in every direction, and do not move forward or backward, or sideways, and the one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: for fear it would contract
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one who is at the top or on the forehead, make the skin flat with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and cut into it, then drain it and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large abscesses hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	No time happens in bellies and nowhere else they say, and is a disease that is called “fungus” by the resemblance of those, and is the root subtle, and the head large; and there are small and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a fine root, and they were slightly split open, and pus came out of them
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 ounces, and the work on incision is that you see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artichoke is white and moist and of fine root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the cut is to the hip bone wide, and in your presence be the fire cautery. For at the cutting comes many times too great bleeding, and if the blood does not stop, then hasten therefore to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient fearing and afraid of the incision with iron, then take one thread of linen well made, and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the linen thread until it heals the joint, and let it cure by itself without work. And if the roots are large, then fear to cut even the belly, but you can well cut half;
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the flesh which is of pale color and poor sense and of milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an abscess festering, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is healed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the wound comes from a cautery of a cut or fissure of the skin, and is on the abdomen and has no boils as it may have in other wounds, or blood coming from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the rupture of the skin and the exit of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open to various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when it is pressed to its sides, it rises back up, and then returns, and by chance, it may be tightened, and enlarges much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it at all; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is for windiness, it is puffed up when touched, and the workings are that you look to see if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary that you leave the care. Because there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in this chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, it is necessary that you command the patient to hold his arm, and be stretched straight, then seize all around the boil.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	Then command him to press firmly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have seized with all the spatula.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then is half of the abscess above to the whole great incision
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the wound be closed
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work the half of the abscess extended on the thread, and put your index finger in, and search
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught by the thread, then untie it, and bring the intestine out to the outside of the belly
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the boil, then take it at the root, and cut away the superfluity
