et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go well around it, and then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a crosswise way so that you make it pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then tighten the abscess on four leagues above the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave them there until it pusses, and let the dead flesh come away by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Or you cut it when it is subtle and suppurating, then treat it as is proper, and cover the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or the moisture that you find, then cure the place of it as it is required, and solder the place.
dou chancre	about the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of ulcers, and how one should work on them with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and let us say that ulcers are created in the marshes, and great caution is needed in their treatment, and ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped like an ulcer that is in the nipples, and in the groin, and similar places, and it should be completely removed when it is at its beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not appropriate that you approach it, because I have never healed any of them; nor has anyone else ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then prepare the patient's skin well to perform the operation; then cut out your ulcer or sore, and shave it all around, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and press the place firmly with your hand or any other thing, and if the flow of blood goes against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the appearances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; so it is only enlightened; and one must not touch with iron in these two appearances: namely, tympanites and hyposarches, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this appearance of dropsy which is called "enlightened" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as gout and solution of the belly and similar things; if you do not touch with iron because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	lift the patient straight up with your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the lower abdomen, then take the spine spatula according to this form: And be sharp in two parts. At the point, and nonetheless it should not be so deep that it can come until the intestine when one inserts it, and you cannot pierce it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is hindered towards the intestines: then it behoves that you split below the belly three fingers straight under the armpit; and if the dropsy is from the sickness of the liver, then let the incision be on the left side of the belly three fingers; and if it is from the spleen, then to the right, and it behooves not that the patient lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow to the weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the spout, and lift your hand to all the spatula between the skin and the syfac as much as when you are scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or a bit more; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the point eight, and this is the place of the water, then the water flows out, and you remove this instrument from which this form is: And it resembles a fine silver chain, and it is of light iron or steel, and on the lower part one small hole; and where it costs on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it descends now on the instrument; empty therefore half or one-third, for if you empty more than behooves in this hour, by adventure the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit of the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but in emptiness according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to those that the dispositions of the virtue of the sick person signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now for the heart which stops the passage which is on the syfac, because I have spoken of this, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin again the instrument the other day, if you see the sick person suffering those, and treat of the water a small quantity.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this no day, and keep yourself from watering until it does not remain but a little of water. And if you doubt about the sick person, and you give him much water, then cure him with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bath and in the sun, and he is stained to drink; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. If this is so, it should be immediately examined to see if it can be pierced with a very fine spatula according to this form: then put a clo, that is, a fine plug of lead, into the opening, and tie it and hold it for three or four days and when he wants to urinate, have him remove the plug and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps this will not work, because the urine which comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose opening is small, if they are medicated with the lead plug, as we have said, it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its place are blue, because none are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot reach the urethra, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies supine on his back, and they support the head of the penis and the scrotum as if it were a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should; and beware of bleeding which often comes from it, and if it happens, have someone who stanches blood stanch it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come in the penis, and it is a bad appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it behooves you to pick them with one fine needle, and scrape and cleanse them all, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment on top; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blister is malignant, of putrid color and odor, then it behooves you to cauterize it. When you have scraped it, and if the blister is in the head of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it behooves you to remove the blister that is inside first; and when it is healed, then cure the outside one. For when you cure them together, it is not certain that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come in its penis and scrotum; so it behooves to cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made of the bark of quince trees and vetives on top, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, then cauterize with the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauteries help with two dispositions together: that is to say, for bleeding and for corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then it behooves you to put or conduct a chain of lead from the penis, and urinate the patient among; and when the skin is sore at the tip of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then it behooves you to scrape it with one sharp instrument, until the ligatures are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all parts;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a grievous thing to discuss these, then you must cauterize it with a spatula at the point of the head of the staff and the hair; then separate gently between two, and put one subtle drape of linen moistened in cold water so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in terms of continuity; however, when we do this work of our will, and properly to children, it is necessary that we make the best possible work and the most light for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the most greatest part of the masters and the healers who made circumcision around .i. dal, and as forces, and to one whole novacule; if it was the keurs for he has .ij. toiles, and by adventure if one chops this above and remains that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is convenient to cut, and is the pain double, and to the purification which is dou dal is not assured the tip of the member; and to the purification of the knuckle by adventure escapes the iron, and runs the work, and many times they are born as if they do not need purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made as forces to all the linen of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, so evenly in .i. all tighten; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you only tie the thread around the rod so much, and then let him move it in every way that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make him stand straight between your hands, and bring the forces between your hands or below your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the rod and blow out his breath, and draw it upward until the head of the rod is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it below .i. point to .i. other thread; and hold it as .ij. points by the second binding to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the .ij. bindings, then lift his breath upward gently and draw the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood come out point and point, because it is the medicine; and put powder on top and on top of the powder .i. drapeil glued with a mixture of a boiled egg whites tempered with rose water, confited with rose oil good and fresh, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures as long as he is cured.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces to the mundification is this: the two shoulders are held and are pointed, and the shoulders are also as large as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the pliers inside are at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger so that the lead makes an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then take tongs, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pierce for .iij. days, and what is below the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscess has calmed, and lightly peel it; then cut as much as you can move, and guard the part of the rod, it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things suddenly wound with powder, that we have said or treated about powders, and if one cuts too much with the pliers, and it goes upwards, it will not harm; cure therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from an obstruction of the stone, or of congealed blood, or of a bowel, or of new flesh, or similar things, which we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the bladder neck, then it behooves the patient to be bent on his knees; and let their feet be placed on the back, and extend his belly from above the back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it behooves you to administer extraction with all the instrument that is called "syringe," of which this is the form: and let it be of fine silver, light, shaped like a bird's feather; and let the handle be a palm long and a half, and let it be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take one double thread, and tie at the chief one pock of wool or cotton, and put the chief of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the chief of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and water tede;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then put lightly the syringe in the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the bud; then put the syringe forward up to the bladder, and feel the patient come until the thing empty, and this is not done according to this order further than because of that which conducts or where it goes is twisted; then there is the thread at all the wool pock and pock, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and begin again the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scalds or blood comes in the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see it distilling waters and medicines, so do it with all the instrument which is called "clepsydre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has .iij. openings: .ij. on one side, and .i. on the other, as you see; and its lips curve so that the medicine stays such that it well stops the penis without addition, so that if one can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you wish to put your medicines in the bladder, place the chief of the  kettle into the moisture, and draw with the tube which is inside; so draw the moisture to the kettle, and then firmly push back the tube inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or of pewter, and the head is higher; and below it .i. finger's width or the length of the arm; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture with which you wish to enema the bladder, then tie it between the .ij. breasts formed with a double strong cord, and heat .i. handful of that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the anus, then strain your hand on the bladder with all the moisture coming in, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you don't have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make .i. circle out of it, and pierce it roundly all around; then put .i. strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like one assembles .i. dart, and put inside that which you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it onto the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, by pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work by size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens more to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears hard, and pains the patient's penis, and he feels it many times, and then becomes soft; and with many of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light the healing of children until they have four years, and it is very painful in the elderly, and is as the middle for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by clyster, to draw out all the feces which are in the intestines. For it often obstructs anything seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and dislocate them and move down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it comes out once from its place above; then make him sit between your hands properly, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then the one side and touch it from within.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone. And if it does not fall at the touch of all, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and push it into its base, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, pull it to the neck of the bladder; then press upwards on your finger, and push it outwards where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then push the spatula cutting, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between that which is between the buttocks and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be right over the stone, and the two sides should be even or foundation, and let the loincloth be so that it's wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press so the two sides that are or foundation, that it jumps outward without work; and know that there is such stone where it has angles, and margins: if it is cut to go through; and if it is like a ball, round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that one then where it has angles and margins, make the loincloth larger; and if it doesn't jump, it is necessary that you extract it with tweezers that are also like a file at the head, to move extract the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you put under it 1 instrument subtle curved at the head; and if you cannot engineer it this way, then enlarge 1 pock the opening, and if it is without decortication, then strain with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	and if there are more than one stone, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then the track forward, and the small ones after if there are more. And if it is very large, it should be removed, and make a larger wound. Because two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes back through where the urethra cannot close; but nevertheless try to drain it, or to break it with tweezers, until you pull it out in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, smear the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and restrain it, and put on top one cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandaging until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, cleanse the area well with oil and water, then treat it with diaphicon ointment and basil ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and clotting of blood in the bladder, and because of this retained urine, which is known in such manner that without going out with the urine: then you must put all things in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound of water and air and soil, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you care for him, you bind his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the urethra leads, and it is stuck there, and the urine cannot pass; so cure in this way as I said before, that you enlarge it many times, it is an excuse for enlargement by this treatment. I have already proven it this way.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron according to this form and be three corners hooked into one stick:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then insert the rod into the rod lightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand at the stone point by point, until you can feel the stone on the other side; soon urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the rod. Then it is broken, and it jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above, then make the rod straight towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, untie the threads, and cleanse the congealed blood which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that a stone is engendered in women, and if it happens at any time, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for .iij. things: one is that by chance the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowing woman who will uncover herself to look at the stones, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is so much deeper than the stone of the man, for which reason it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you procure a wise woman well-knowing, and at pains the true one is found, and if you cannot find her, then no chaste woman of subtility; and present to her a wise person in the affairs of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look well if the woman is a virgin: then she must put her buttocks or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she constricts it below her buttocks, and recommends that she puts her buttocks or on the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it from great to small from the entrance of the bladder until below, as long as it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttocks, where it appears mued and felt the stone in that part; and do not move her buttocks above or below the stone, and let the tail be first small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then put the root in the tailbone, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as long as the stone can be pushed out, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins. If you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the stone pains, put ground vitriol on it, and hold it there for an hour until the pain is extinguished; then return to your work, as long as the stone remains firm, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones for men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone pains, and it is from the artery that is cut, put the powder on the spot and strain with bandages and cloth, and do not begin again those, and let the stone and do not touch it, lest the patient die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the limbs are numb, then return to your work, as long as the stone remains firm.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous ramice is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is the substance from the center of the testicles that contains the egg; and it is called “syfac,” and at times it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is i.e., another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and those have this point not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors:  it is either yellowish declining towards jaundice, or red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, so is the abscess re-formed, that is, round like the figure of an egg, and does not open the openings, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper cloth, so is the abscess re-formed with a part of the egg, and for this one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the openings and the white as such, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you must examine the entire introducer  quarrel, of which the form is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of this which is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his strength and the repletion of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put under him much of cloths;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart from the sides;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the sides between them from their long side up to near the armpit, and let your incision be straight, dividing the skin of the sides until it reaches the white marrow, and flay it carefully according to your strength;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the abscess with pure water to one inch wide openings, and extract all the pus, and then put on your bandages, and raise the abscess; and do not touch the tip of the points, but only the abscess; cut all or in pieces evenly the edge of it subtly, that if you do not cut it well skillfully, the pus will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has healed in your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the abscess; then assemble the two leaves of the tip of the points with a suture, and cure it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the ulcer corrupted by another malady, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the flowing of blood; then cut the point to all the suspender, and extract the ulcer, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the fluid is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part just as you have done the first evenly, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound clean linen moistened in rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put over another linen moistened in wine and oil, and place the two pads on top, and put blankets over them, and tie them above all the linen according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use them as padding according to this appearance and be joined by stitching in the groin of the breeches, and one of the thighs lies on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the armpit; and the other two from the head above the two angles, and let the entire restraint be assembled in the buckle of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this root of cautery is medicated in place of a knife of iron, and that you take one subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the genitals, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac which contains the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac with one incision, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cut in all ways that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salved; and moves guarding against a drop of blood, and moves less than the works of the knife;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing opposes you, or abscess or discharge of blood or any other thing, so care for what opposes you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer a piercing as I have told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that a watery root is there,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of all the spatula wide, and put the piercing long into the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water may flow out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the place, and bind it, and leave for it to run out the rest of the water, then treat it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not allow water to flow into the mouth of the wound, it is necessary that you pour in a quill or instrument with which one treats the water of those who are hydrophic, of which the form is as before; and enlarge i. poc the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after .vj. months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this vein there is fear in more than one disposition, so it seems to me better that it be left.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the joints; and this is for many reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say by excess of sour and sharp, which is spread to the joints, or from percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it finds no pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance some abscesses are fierce and painful and of dark color, and sometimes comes from out of an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, then it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it should not be touched at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	That one which is made from a swelling of a vein is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers,
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can do well to cut along this manner, and on other limbs;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then the leaf is on top, and the stalk is white, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the leaf.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the leaf is already cooked with these new limbs, then you must pull out the leaf, and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is airy to the stalk, or in that which is inside the vessels, then you must deliver all of that membrane and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is at the rear or front, it behooves you to cut it entirely, and remove the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the works are accomplished, then apply the wound to wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cover it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed in a covering resembling that of a certain onion, with the softening of the testicles.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	And the patient moves sharply when he goes;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	And the cure of this illness is as well prescribed as that previously mentioned.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on one elevated seat, then put the suspender of the loincloth down to his heels,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	To all the vessels which are near the penis, and the masters braid them, and stretch them.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	Then cut with the sharp spade widely through the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	And then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then place a needle where it has one double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein came, and tie it straight to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut the sinews in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and treat the rotten moistures.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then cure the wound as with others where one prevents bowing, so that no vessel be seen that nourishes one of the corners.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	Because by those no evil comes, and to all vessels blood comes, it is necessary to treat the corners of all vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	So that the flesh does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dries out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hip
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this malady is by the section that comes at the hip, or by the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either at the hip or of its extension, and these two ways of bad come from many causes: whether by percussion, or jump, or by straining, or lifting a heavy load, and similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of the extension of the hip are that there is a poke and poke, over a long time, and does not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal until near the edge because the pus presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the pus, that it brings a sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear diverse, under the skin near, and this because of the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the pus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes these (abscesses) touch with the intestine, and are held in, and cause great pain to suffer to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, because it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to push the intestine into its place in the wound, if it can enter.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either support it under his collarbone between your hands, and raise his hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the chest upward, and cut all the skin of the groin long;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push inside the folds of the waist tweezers according to what you need to open the wound, and make it such that the intestines can issue out;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape away the surface skin that is under the skin of the buttocks, until the white underlying layer is uncovered from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then insert your index finger into that which follows the buttock, in what is between the white layer beneath the skin of the buttocks and between the second layer.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And separate that which is behind the buttocks and between the second layer. And then move with your right hand into the center of the buttocks, and have the white layer on top to your left hand, and lift the buttock onto all the layers towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister to extend the buttock upwards, and loosen that which is behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask your two if it has any point of the intestine enveloped or white hard thing, and if you find none of these things, push it to the belly below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle or it has one large thread made of ten threads, and put it in the rear part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the buttock; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear of the threads, until there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the syfac, which we said is below the skin of the buttock, with a strong thread of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the hairs of the threads, and tie them together forming two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter in, except for an abscess coming there.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put directly the linen according to the first linen long two spans of that one, and after these two linens leave down from the side which is under the heart of the groin the large one of a span.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the groin, as much as the sinew, and the bone, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it on the wounds, and there administer the linen that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the white groin that we have said cauterized after the incision, out of fear of a decrease in blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and let the thread remain as long as it comes out through it; and if it delays in coming out, so be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it comes out.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this practice, I never saw anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch that is assembled to the vine, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who work, as long as the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	At times a rupture comes in the angles, as we have said, and apart their limbs; and do not send any of the intestines to the groin, and if any are sent there, it is bad, and repair them all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nonetheless if it remains too long in this point, the wound or syphilis grows, as long as the intestine is sent.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the extension of the sinew which is at the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and inflamed its ends and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure of this is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies sideways on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated with a width according to the quantity of three finger widths;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then pull out the sinew which is under the skin that it follows, then take the lead and put it on the place appearing of the sinew;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press on the front of the belly, then cut the two appearing joints of the thigh on the head of the thigh bone, and cut each one.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then extract the head of the thigh bone, and do not cut any of the thigh nor extend any other thing, as I have told you in the treatment of the intestinal hernia;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then treat it by the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the filaments, if it has a hole and cleans the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The thigh is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles softens in certain men, because the contents within are softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin which is softened over the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you see it, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and tie the thread.
dou chastrement	of the cauterization
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that cauterization is commonplace in our law, and for this reason, I would like to not speak of it much in this book; it is necessary only in two ways: one is so that the healers know how to respond when asked about it and how to cure it; and the other because we often need cauterization of certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and calves and other animals. I therefore say that cauterization is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. In the one we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles are softened and pliable; then taking them with your hand, hold them until they are pulled back and you no longer feel them.
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodite is according to .ij. ways as men: the one if it is that between the .ij. sexes open as well as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine.  And the other manner is in women, and has on the groin as well as a penis and .ij. sexes. And the cure of the man and of the woman is that you cut the joined parts all, and cure them as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.
