Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a joined part on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. It behooves you to trim the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or tongs, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, that bleeding does not come, then the cure of other cures until it is healed; and to another part that is born at the mouth of the privates, and the groin, and by chance leaps forth, and is according to the semblance of a cow, and for this reason they call it the ancients "cow disease". If you should cut it, as we have said the tenting, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	of erratic if is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident by illness that came to it; or it is by char ajoined, or by syfac subtle or thick, and it is made in the groin, or in ribs, or below, or where it may be; and prevent conceiving, and childbirth, and by adventure the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these is by the regard of the bailey. If the stoppage is near appearing, if you will at your two sides or to the rear. If it is of subtle syfac, and it is near the .ij. leivres, then hurry, and thus: put your .ij. sides together, and let the woman be on her back, legs spread; then are the .ij. leivres formed, as long as the subtle syfac is round, and is over the stoppage; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and lie the woman to her husband each day, so that she cannot stir. And if the syfac is hard and thick, then you must cut it with the spatumile seeming like a myrtle leaf. If the stoppage is of char born, then suspend it to the  and cut; and have the medicines that staunch blood, as com acaice, dragon's blood, incense, together abundant of egg; then administer a caine of large plonc, so that the wound may not join; and thus long, and administer her a tent of dry linen; then be cured with other cures until it is healed.  And when in the groin comes char born, then it must be cut according to this manner, if it is not abscesses enchancrez. For the abscess enchancreit that is in the groin, one should not touch to do.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thul; and we have said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those who resolve healing. I say that hemorrhoids and the thul, when they are em-formed in the marshes, and they do not appear to smell, except for the cure by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel, are those one can cure. Thus it is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then after the thul is seized with tongs, and the cut in its roots, then powder with medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the air for one hour, then put her in cold water; and if she decorates from blood, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranate and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confide it with honey and aisil, and make .i. plaster on her back. And if it is healing, it is good. If it is not, then make her suck wind suction cups on the back and breasts without hurting; then take linen, and moisten it in plantain juice or in elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the place. And when the abscess rests, cure its place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called «albathir» is red, and is similar to .i. asp chief, so one must cut it as I said the thul; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marshes
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marshes, such as chancre and purulent abscesses and herpes and estiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and more other diseases that I have said in the division. Thus it is necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the marshes, which is not of the abscesses that coil bowel; and if you want to know the work of iron, see whether the abscess is aged at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.  Therefore do not haste to pierce it, but let it die until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a .i. seat, and have .ij. small seats where he leans, and support his back and bring his feet to the parts further from the leg; and be his hips spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good linen; then suck him sideways towards the right side, and administer the instrument that works the mouth of the marsh, so that which comes after. And it is necessary that when you see administering this instrument, that you first stick its tip in to know the depth of the marsh, so that what enters inside the instrument does not come deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marsh with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt them; and it is necessary that he puts the cone of the instrument on top, and that he holds the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and you feel it with your hand soft, then it is necessary to cover it at the head, at the spatumile leit; and when the bowel is emptied, it is necessary that you put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in green oil sec; and put the tent further from the wound to the depth of the marsh, and put further over the marsh and over the loin cloth clean moistened in water or malves are cooked; then cure it after .ij. days of ointment coming before this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the marsh and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and long aristoloch being cooked; then return to the ointment. And if the wound is renewed in the marsh, it is necessary that you guard against iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first important to the midwife that she know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pushing downward, and desiring to smell the air: then the fetus hastens to issue forth; therefore, you know that this childbirth is according to nature's figure, and is the head first and the buttocks with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the fetus issues forth quickly; for when it ascends onto its head, then the buttocks come with it, and the woman is delivered of her superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fetus comes forth on its head by natural delivery, and the woman is laboring hard, and her strength is weak, then make her sit upon a saddle, or let the women hold her up; and anoint her behind with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs, the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the secondine, and chop it at its nail until the moisture that is inside is gone; and press the woman's belly as much as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clyster of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her take and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: so now the child will come out. And if the two hands issue forth, then it is necessary that you gently pull them back and forth; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up; then tip the stool over onto the ground, and hold onto the woman, so that she does not fall during the tipping; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then chop the hands at the knife which is previously put, and extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	from the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on its feet, then it is necessary to push it upwards.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then he turn it back and forth, until it is even
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then prick the place and stretch it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	It can jump up to the hips, if he commands to take it, and make it sneeze with condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come healed as we have said, then take a handful of alder, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind everything in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put on the inside of the woman's natural orifice and outside this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make him sit upright until under the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened below, make him one collar of mire and put it below, and let it stand an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make him sit on a seat, then make him sneeze and restrain his mouth and nose, and take hold of his belly lightly, for the child leaps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands poke and poke.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	Then be supported on his neck, and the legs dangling down, and lying on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	And he bends his hands poke and poke, and then he takes the hands on his belly, and he pulls the cushions under so that she is prepared down.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the child doesn't jump, he takes his legs and moves them forcefully, then he moves the belly upward, then he pushes with his hands.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and rock the child back and forth; and command the woman to stay still until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child which comes out with a broad hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then have the woman rise and leave.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it cannot go, so make a bed on i.e. a lit, and the legs are formed.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	Then administer the muscle ointment that I have recounted;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if she doesn't give birth, so make her sit on i.e. a seat, then study to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And guide the child according to the natural figure, and make her sneeze, and command her to lie down as long as the child is there.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on his neck, and has spread his hands, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is fitting that the midwife holds her hand, then turns it little by little, and the arm lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, she places it on the soft, fleshy part of the arm and oil, as we have said, then she commands her to move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make her sit on one seat and command her to sneeze. And the girl sneezes.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all of the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to treating in this way to all of the spine, so grasp the spine with your finger, as long as the moisture is emptied;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child can rise on his face and on his neck, so grasp from the base, that it is not held, and die the child;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then throw the child inside, as long as you have put him as it is right, and command to the woman that she take no care at any time;
adonques si istra legierement.	therefore, it must be gently reset.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and they do not live, if one is named;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they are multiplied, and are severed by the faculty which divides them, which is joined to the head.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and at times they come forth as naturally as one under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come forth with force, then the cure is as we have said, and let the physician be subtle and make it quickly and easily.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as he deems to salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	At no time are they formed in the marshes, i.e., one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of their glorious sage,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the bailiff know all this, because by chance similar things happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so that it be done according to what is proper.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands.
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she fears death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	then it is necessary that the woman be positioned on her back, and her hips inclined downward, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister binds the band of two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it is not treated with the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mare with moistened oils with musk of aloe and fennel and flaxseed, then anoint the bail her hands with these oils and these muscillas.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then put them in the mare lightly, then desire one row where she puts the stitches that be suitable to these,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take ward if the child is appearing that it descends upon his head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	If he places the cauteries in his eyes or neck or mouth or on his palate or under his chin or in the armpit or near the ribs
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on feet, he puts it or pricks and at the middle ribs.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the cautery with his right hand, and puts the curve between his fingers of his left hand, and pushes it with all his hand lightly, and places the cautery in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the void thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the cautery:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert against one other bone, or third if you need it, so that the extraction be equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then make it equal in moving from one side and the other, so that it may fit easily, and let the bones be toothed to hold, as this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if there remains a part, then apply some of its oil to the ankle, and put it in that part, and draw the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if none remains, then put this bone or higher up, and do this until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then it is necessary that you envelop it in a cloth, until it sets;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then bind it at the joint of the root or to the cut, and in this way you must do with the other hand, and for two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's shoulder is swollen and it is inflamed at its opening, or if it has an acute ache assembled,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it is necessary that you put the pointed spatula between your two, and make the chief and extract the water.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	Or you have it with the instrument which is called “almidach,” so that its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And in the same way make it if the infant has a great head naturally.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	And then pull out the bones with the pliers,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head of the shoulder leaps and is forced, it must be split as much as the moisture which is there or worse has issued.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it as much as the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the cavity is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stuck in the belly or the breast, then you must draw it out with i.e., a cloth wrapped around the hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture that is in it corrects itself;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other members are removed, and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then bring the healer's hand from the root of the marrow, and pull it up to the mouth of the marrow;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he puts one or two, and the treatment will follow.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the abscess is retracted because of a hot boil that has come, it does not need to be worked.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then it is necessary to administer moist and fatty things.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and he administers plasters, and soak in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, then administer what we have said in the living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if one has no power over it, then the body should be treated in pieces, and nothing of the second part should be left.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said concerning abscesses that come in the marshes.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if discharge of blood comes, then put it in water restraining, and administer other treatments to it.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been stillborn, then conceived another upon that one, and miscarried the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time she had an abscess in the wound, and it swelled so much that it opened and began to drain greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a strong adhesive plaster upon it, and after some days one bone came out, and after some more days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because this one whose belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I touched the wound, and in my hands were bones, until the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived a long time thus, and it seemed to have a little bit of bowel from there;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter only for those who, when masters find a strange thing, they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the forceps, how it is made in books; and at two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictive [part], and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the tube be i.e. two of wide, and the margin of the trees i.e. must, and long one palm and half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the middle of the two limbs be two adjustments of this same tube, which are fastened in one and the other, of half palm of long or a poke more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two adjustments are put in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood tube, according to the likeness of pliers;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two heads of two joints, as you see, an arm's length long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see to open the veins with all the instrument, make the woman sit on one bed, her feet hanging and her legs open,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two joints together in the vein, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then operate your hand on the instrument as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the vein, as long as the woman does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all mounted and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the eyes have appeared them, so much more hasty is the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is held during childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her breath, and then have her sneeze from condiment, and restrain her hands to her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps for this, well and good.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not work, take one pot and make one hole or cover it, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamine, rue, anise, chamomile, cassis, and wormwood.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or none of them, be cooked or put in water on the fire; then put one end of the rope or hole into the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And steam it until the vapor comes from within the marsh; then let it be exhaled, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second part jumps hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more force, command the midwife to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in the ointment of alum, and then put it in the opening.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And grasp the second one; and when she has found it, grip it and extend it little by little straightly, so that the uterus does not fall during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	But it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the opening of the uterus is too narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	And if it is not from all of what we have said, then guard that you do not use for milk.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	But it is necessary that the one who is at the mouth of the mare, you bind him to the hip of the woman, then the clysterize of ointment tetrafarmacon.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the woman will bear and put it back, and come forth well; but nonetheless, when she bears it then comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and pales the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary fumigations suitable for that: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the second thing is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is in the form of a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let the fumigation be on the coals, and the tinder as long as it is burned, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	to consider its foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, but it is stopped by some subtle things.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So it befits the midwife that she pierces that thing to its proper place, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guards the incision so that she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then care for the ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not close up again, then put on a poultice of flax, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go into the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from a swelling of a wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that swelling: if it is cured, as we have said of the cautery of pitch.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the fundament are knotty, and larger than those that come from beside the fundament outside, or in the space of two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is a fistula or more than one; and when that knotting is old, it works, and still moisture arises white or subtle pus,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are personal; and they are known by those who have them or when there is evacuation or windiness when the patient evacuates, and by chance one leaps to others.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and reach to the joint of the groin, and to the root of the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula piercing at the base, and not piercing:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you thrust your two index fingers or foundation, and thrust a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has curvature, put a tent of fine lead or one hair of a horse, as long as you feel the tent or hair to your touch.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it, and it does not come out with difficulty or windiness or moisture, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	Know that it does not pierce at all; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or to the urethra, if it leaks urine and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced up to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes to that place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no torsion and the pain is in the surrounding area, then it is that it has a twist, and it does not merit medicine or treatment by ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these fistulas Persians have no other cure except labor, and vanity of the fools who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those which are neither Persian nor ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, as far as you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the foundation, then you must put your index finger there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you feel that the tent has pierced it; and whether uncovered or you feel between your finger the soft tissue or cartilage, then you know that it is through.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	However, one can heal some well, but this rarely happens.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help one gives them, if it is to cauterize with subtle fire according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and burn the whole thing hot in the fistula, until it reaches the base; and do this 2 or 3 times, as long as you know that these charcoaled things are burned, which resemble an ostrich feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure of tents moistened in butter, as long as that matter will issue forth, then the cure of ointment closing up flesh and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, it is well. If this one, otherwise it cannot be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your bottom and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or of silk, and you see the fistula at this one which follows the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the tent, and then the cauterize after, as long as it comes to the top of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and will be delivered the tent, and it will fall; then cut those feathery things that seem like a bird's feather, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood vein goes wrong, and it comes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery combines two good things: namely, the burning of those attached veins, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure with tents soaked in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as their pus flows, and until the burned veins are pulled out of the wound;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then heal the wound of inflammations quickly by applying dry hard flesh, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the root of the foundation, and is removed from the body, then you put your finger or foundation there, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent and between two or three is the fabric or the syfac or chars, where it is near to piercing, then there is no other way except by means of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put a tent and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not cut too deep, that you do not cut the tissue which holds the base, and let the secretions come out by the natural will.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	and perhaps it will be healed, or you move that covering and the wound after it is cut near the base, or by tent or other appointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	Then cleanse the scabbed flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation: so it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are like this: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or lies against the foundation next to the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts one thread wrong in two, and puts the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is piercing in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread of that one pierced, just as you put your two or foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to another, and leave it one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no times, until the threads close these cartilages that are between two, and they join;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not become to make for the lacing cover if too deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula spine from which one makes the fistula is very useful, partly and trenching.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, because one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to two ways: or they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short they bleed.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and moreover over a little bit of water clear or a little bit of blood, and have the color of the body
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them within the foundation, if it is that you command the patient to stretch himself so that he go into chambers, until the foundation of him is gone, and the filaments appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hasten, and can grasp it with pliers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tweezers cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take them with one cloth, or cotton, or a piece of felt;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and straigten them to your hands, then cut them, and powder above some hot powders that are in place of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the base cannot be issued, then cleanse the patient with a harsh and sharp enema to wash what is at the base, so that it can be issued openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient endures, and if the threads are far from the base, then the cure is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you prick them with your finger or tongs, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it in a needle, then lead the thread above and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is of a good width; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one to correct the excess of blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation one pad moistened in rose oil or in cerate, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let him be until they heal, and when they are cured, treat them with ointments and other treatments until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying up of veins in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then you should resort to the point of a spatula or your fingernail to scrape off the peel above, so that it does not become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it until it is healed as it should
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, begin the scraping again more forcefully than before, until it heals well, and is scraped
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	when it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Ants are a small appearance formed before the body, and go much into it.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes they find them cold, and one feels them also like dead from shivering, and it comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a candle of an ostrich feather, or a raven's feather strong, and put that candle on the shivering, until the circle surrounds the shivering completely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to the whole candle until you cover the whole shivering, and put it in, and root out the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this of a dog of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and long above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, for must keep to the two, and move pressed And if you see, so cauterize the edge, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time made one enema of silver or lead, or iron melted or woven; and no time is made of these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those who are administered in the cure of the children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, small and large, so it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner.
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is pierced inside; and on one side are .ii. holes, and on the other .i.;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and it is the belly where one puts the medicines of a bladder of beast or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And between each puncture one must put space, then place in these punctures one strong thread of cruet twisted thread in ten or as it may turn, and assemble the belly like a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside, then tie the ligature in front with a strong thread, then administer an enema; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and grease the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk or something similar, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the minister squeezes it with his two hands together until it is all emptied, then withdraw the enema, and have the patient raise his legs to the side,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to spread, so let the hair as much as it can; and if it sleeps one night altogether, so it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him in the sickness of belly falling, and the medicine hastens to spread, so begin again until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or abscess, so let the enema be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin is restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of stone, and the cutting of sword and knife, or of lance or staff or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or what are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head simple, because remembrance comes in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if it takes care if it is of a stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt heavily of an abscess hot: if it becomes quite healthy from the cephalic itself even if it comes little blood from the wound, and if the healthy is on the contrary side of the wounded;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient from filling with wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat be less, and drink no wine, nor eat any flesh;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in wine stiptce;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh and all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the art has moved it, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tenting, then assemble them by stitching, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to bone, and it's hanging loose and holds only by a thread, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in its place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat large meats, like beef and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a rotting skin, and it does not reach the bone, so cut all of the rot away, and throw it out, then cure;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if it has an artery in the wound or vein, which does not close with a ligature, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie up the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that you put into this powder which binds as soon as the arsenic has healed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place, until it dries well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then cover it well, and leave it without removing it, unless it swells; for the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the heat has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has healed the wound, even if it is still open, do not put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some medicinal unguents, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it is healed.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you here afterward the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if it has no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it to heal, and put nothing restraining upon it, because it harms the nerves and causes them to retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put on the wound anything cold, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be warm, such as calx washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cupped wash also in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it and bind it with bandages, then tend to it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of boil, then pierce or lower them.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and blood flows, then staunch it, and tie it up, and cauterize as necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the airway is guarded, so that the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	Then sew the heart on the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but place it back according to its natural form;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then the strain happens to them frequently, and leave him for a few days, then cures with ointments drying until it is healed
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then so it will.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, treat them fiercely all that you can, and those that you cannot get, leave until the wound suppurates.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and make it free and align the opening;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look if from the wound there is windiness as the patient strains;  then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it at all for the blood not to settle in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return it to the heart, and apply a bandage to the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture;
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if no spasms come, nor bad heart tremor nor twitchings of the arm;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good arrangements, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it then with bandages and other dressings, as long as he is healing;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and work, know that there is a fistula there; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, treat it as those in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, suture it; and if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it is deeply embedded in the bone, and has chipped pieces, then close the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not loose, leave the wound to rot, so it will lighten the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	about the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The displacements of the belly are great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Of the great wound there is sometimes protrusion of the intestine, or the nerve of the intestines, by which the intrusion of others;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the suture is more troublesome, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for this reason, intestines are put back in place more easily if they are put back in warm after warm;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they go back in place less easily.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason, a small wound is worse, because for this reason intestines are reset to their place more than other wounds.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is in .iiij. ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The .ij. common sutures happen in the suture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	And the suture of other wounds of the body and .ij. other proper sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And nonetheless they are more clean with the suture of the belly, and I will say one each and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines has emerged,
