et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if it is necessary to put something back in, then this is done in one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Soak a sponge or linen cloth in hot water alone,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook it in water with squashing and cypress and spice,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and apply the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at no time has this been done restraining, and it is moved that it alone for to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, if moist the intestine with water or wine and the leaves be cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by these is aligned the entrance to a little thing.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter there, then make an opening in the wound with the instrument of which one uses to cut hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to move the waist
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut there except with great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut inside the curve and not outside, and look here at the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails have leapt out.
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	If you put it back according to its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, because this is very important.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and buttocks higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	And also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you set your attention on that which the sunken part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is fitting to administer what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds put that which has appeared to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have between your hands  one minister pitiful that keeps all the rupture to his hand
et assemble les levres;	and assembles the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of sutures,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and that you pierce a needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then let from the head of the wound i.e., two fingers' width, and put a needle where it has i.e., a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the  siphac,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is underneath the skin inside, as long as you make it pierced from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the two heads of the siphons the four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the strain of a double thread around the needle of 2 parts
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the 2 ends of the wound alignment
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave 1 two of space, and in it place another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread like you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing this according to what you need of needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	as long as all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and are the needles medium-sized, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles pierce all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason they should be shortened;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not right to put the needles too far from the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not cut and open the wound in front of the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the points of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths on the shoulder of the needles to keep them from moving
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them stay until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of suturing with needles is more advisable in small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one needle or two are sufficient
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is so common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two points of the skin and the two points of the fascia together with a needle where there is one strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have pierced these four points together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then thread the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each suture the thickness of a minor two.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture should cover the man
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that a young man had on his belly
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was slashed with a knife
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and was the wound more than a palm wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was of bowels well two palms wide,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine after it had been 24 hours out,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was stitched together up to 15 days, and I cared for it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in one place where one could not find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put half a cloth moistened more on the wound two times a day, and washed it with water and honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and thread it from the outside to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it pierces the core straight through, hold the tip of the thread or where you inserted the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	And make it pierce from the other side, from the inside to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier does furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the seam of one side, and take it up from the other, until the sewing is entirely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of sewing, which Galens says properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like that which any one does, who brings the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the chiefs to the other chief, in such manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	Insert a needle or chief of mirach proximate, and make him feel it only,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two chiefs of syfac;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it felt from the outer part to the inner one,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the two shoulders
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make one of each be examined from the outer part up to that inside, in two other shoulders which are on the opposite side
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common and the best way of stitching
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Galicians say this phrase and no one witnesses it
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each one.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitch more grievous than of the others of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it:
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the skin; then put on the powder of ground charcoal
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the fire has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and stitch up the flesh, and suture the skin, and the muscle.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then care for the wound as you would others until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you lack medicines, apply, as soon as it begins to fester, old cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you do not have need of other medicine for multiple situations while the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not make commonality with principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is fitting that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the angles, and under the buttocks;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	And if he feels pain or rotting in the bowels, and this happens many times.
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If the enemas of black wine are given, and even if the rotting comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it is pierced inside, and know that when it's the large intestine, it's easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "young" cannot heal when it is rotten,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is for the placement of veins that they are, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps from the wound, put it back in as if it were intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it is old and has become worm or black, then you must tie the place that is black so that bleeding does not come from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	Then cut what is between the linen
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And put the two pieces hanging from below the wound part until outside to align the extraction when the bone falls and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and from it there were excretions and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I set about curing him according to what I could, and did not cease to treat him until he was healed, and the bones joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it join, I feared that the patient was ill in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better dispositions, and ate and drank.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said to the experimenters that when he has a small wound in his intestine, it must be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take fresh threads to large testicles, then gather the lips of the wound
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	And when the thread has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that she pulls her mouth together;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then cut the thread, and this will hold so that it cannot be undone,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put one other splint after in that manner as before, until the wound is completely wrapped;
et cout la plaie.	and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the chief (meaning perhaps a boil or abscess) swells in the intestine, and there comes no nuisance to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can tie up the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestinal thread that be much cleaned out,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread i.e. a thread of linen fine twisted
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching of fringes is not forbidden except according to the way of fiancé and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the internal joints, there is nothing but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it opens up, is universally called "fistula,"
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise when it is lifted and bent inwards.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth a knotted, hard, and white, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also lifted like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in a clear jump inwards, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes little, sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is only due to one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of his malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the matter is rotten, and the substance is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	when the medicine is not good in the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late for digestion, and late for health, and inflated by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary that I make you know the cure for fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the bladder or the intestines or the sides
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if such a thing comes to the propertiness of the principal limb and similar parts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the place I have said, and you have faith in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it known, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, if it curves;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then make a circle with a subtle tent of sponge.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the sponge bends to the tortuosity;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula is opened by hand and you cannot well search it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse it by one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture goes from one opening to another and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then carefully search it with your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and whether it is closed up entirely,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask well the patient of the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you will know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the faulty part and the corrupted matter which are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the cure as long as it is healed
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well deep from right place, so it behooves that you cut it as deep as you can
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist tents in a medicinal agué, and put them until the head of the fistula
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is remaining at the bottom
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointment for strengthening healthy flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it away.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve strikes or affects principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so cleanse the king as long as the corruption is completely removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the remaining things with ointment until it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, and returns bent as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone far enough yet:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	If it is discovered and you want as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot arrive there;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other means than to leave to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can draw it out with pliers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture acts against you, and there is no error nor fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it copes with moisture and flesh, and delivers the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place upon the wound something that prevents rotting,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh around the bones has rotted,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and therefore they will have more easily the bones
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you treat only the corruption until the blackness is completely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large portion of it corrupted, and comes up to the flesh of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it befits to be cleaned and covered all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to one man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was one young man about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the matter came to the leg, and was swollen with a large abscess, and had no external cause to open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the surgeon by their foolishness opened it too much so that the abscess opened
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and corrupted a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came a great deal of pus that all rotted and dampened from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a man put care on for two years, and there was no sage in the art of hands
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I came to him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those that were being healed by the punctures to great extent;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and becoming red the body of the youth, and it had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I covered a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I therefore pried it open, and poked in one of the openings until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was that one who appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and I thought there was no other corruption, except for that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And began to restore the wound with medicines soft by long time, and it could not close together.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then I placed it back, and I tried to close the gap.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do so until I placed it around one palm of the bone, and the joint was forced to its whole length.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with remedies; and he became healthy and healed quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to begin the work except for the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For bloodletting is often evacuated, but it was cured entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in the place of the bone a hard cartilage was born, and was of good disposition and had no annoyance nor opposite in anything, neither to go nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one linen cloth, and strain it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct anyone who has it to stretch it upward;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put one other cord of wool thicker than the first cord, and tie it over the flesh which is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and extend the head, so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward;
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh in the place where you want to see it, so that the skin does not cover the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put one splint or a board under the bone so as to cover the rotten flesh
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to be as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be yet another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open at all, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the flesh entirely; then put one splint under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	And then so from one part to another the corruption, and be the silken thread of the corruption i.e. point, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, so cut the corrupted joint, and silken thread the bone where it contains on the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, so there is nothing else than to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is or in the thumb of the hand, or in the thumb of the foot, so it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless it is necessary that you inquire about that corrosion, how it opens to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve do not make you contrary;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisions and threads for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason, it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument that you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can dislocate due to inside or outside causes.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and they are not helpful at all
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by these of death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of member in member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; if you hurry to cover
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the top of the thigh, if you cut it, and do not let him any space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if you cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, if you cut it at the [elbow], and if it passes the knife, then it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it is not worth administering treatment greater than the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And thus do as when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes in the foot, then cut the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up into the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of covering or sewing the limb is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister to the lower ligament, and another minister to the upper ligament,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you cut away the flesh that is between the two ligaments by one span wide, so that the bone be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then cover or so it, and place on each side one drapery of linen, so that the sore does not touch the healthy place
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and may come to the patient another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place thoroughly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or if you put on any restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb wounded with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to one man in his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption first came in his heel of his foot, until it encompassed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corrosion, he raised himself to cover his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And long time after, it returned the corrosion where two of the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things  rebounding after the purification of the body, and could not cease the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted that I cut off his hand, and I would not, because I had hope of rebounding the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and fear also that if he cuts his hand, he will not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the virtue of man was weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and took to covering his hand, and became healthy.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have recounted this tale only because for those who need it, there are others to be made.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to a head in flesh, and remains so long that it causes great collection of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it bursts and pierces, and out pours the pus, and remains like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin that is above is as subtle as one thin linen cloth,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not reach down to the bone nor to the nerve, and such a sickness is called "Sain,"
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called «fistula»;
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so lengthened that it comes to the bone in its entirety, then it is called «fistula»;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure for this is that you cut all around that skin, and also when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and let it not be closed up because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin hardens, and the corruption is not yet complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with this enema:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the breasts are large, and the bowel within them smells bad,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then administer an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take thus, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put to cook in one vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in clysters the groin, and restrain the opening;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain for 2 hours, then remove it squeezing
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the breasts are softened, and fear is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at no time are they to be clystered with water of ashes
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from the vine wood, and pour water over them
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then the flow, and in a clyster, until you know that the breast is well moistened.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then clyster with water and honey where there is a bit of litharge ground;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you clyster it with honey and sweet wine, that the honey may have the property of purifying and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes the healthy drunk;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clyster made of what causes flesh to be born in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and that you apply a plaster of diaphram, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you can medicate him with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken about the properties or treating ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of his chest is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter there,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then widen it with iron a bit, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilican ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, so leave it just as much space where the clyster can enter
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the opening that lies above is lower, then cut or more below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in its entirety, do not leave any entrails inside.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cut below the breast as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it is set up in such a manner that the bow comes to the lowest place that there is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bow is fully extended, if there is no cartilage left
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breastbone as you see fit,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	if it is set up in such a manner: that the bow comes lightly down, and nothing of the bow is left;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take solidifying medicines to put on the chest,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and are placed over i.e., a linen cloth that covers the whole chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then close with force the opening of the chest i.e., somewhat larger than the first
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply ointment suffused on another cloth according to the quantity of the opening,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and it is placed on the opening of the chest to align the rib, and do not remove the large drapery outside except after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And the one who is out of the opening of the chest, is often removed to remove the rib,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes from the rib, whether it's venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed if the patient feels pain or none, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been spread out in this manner and you see nature leaping on top of the wound
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast will close soon, and approach the health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then untie it in the morning, or at midday, and when you untie the wound
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change one other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed indigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venoms cut after a long time, so do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health approaches. For there are men whose wounds heal slowly in their flesh, and some who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if a breast lies bowed, indigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the chest takes long to heal, and is swollen, then apply medicines drying moist in substance and drying in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as ointment of diaphnetis, because it contains a large portion of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take ointment of diaphnetis, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then confit it and use it; and the same made honey well cooked enclose (them);
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When a swelling does not disappear
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take mire and aloe and incense, and grind it, and sprinkle it on the honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then put it in cloth, and place it on the chest, and once administered one long ruler
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lilies celestial, which is also as flour of quince and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or composites: grind them, and make it into powder, and put on top of the honey that I said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is lengthened, and is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then you know that corruption is deep in it, and makes impression on the bone, or hard members, or limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A carbuncle is an abscess that arises under the finger joint of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or in the foot, or by chance arises in other parts;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and one does not take care of it, then there comes one abscess after another,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And they will run and twist the bone as long as they run to the root of the joint, and perhaps they run it all the way.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corrosion comes to the bone until there is pain and it is the shoulder twice as wide, and the color is purple.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut with iron all the superfluity which is remaining from the joint,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail follows the flesh inward, and it begins to prick and blister,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put the root under the nail that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the top end, and cut this carefully and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put above the remaining of the meat medicinals hot and corrosive to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out, and treat it further, for as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the bone corrupted, cut it in one of its parts as it has been said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken and swollen, and causes great pain, then you must first heal it;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the bone with a spatula by cutting across from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And guard that the tail does not come near the flesh which is below the angle, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the source from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is sometimes where there are bones, and some time there is a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in no one of us two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born in neither of our two does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the joint of the two, by chance may move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Waist it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, so is grievous to cure; so keep you from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or should be at the last buttock, it is necessary that you cut first the fleshy rounding until the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then bind the bone to a suitable cloth then care for it until it is healed
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sutures that come as two together come from birth, or from the soldering of a wound, or from the burning of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you bind that suture so that the parts return to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil so that they do not adhere.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you put between two pieces of subtle plank, until the wounds are soldered together, as is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The soldering comes to none of his two with the palm, if it copes that soldering as is fitting.
Des vils	Of villains
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Those are veins large wrapped full of melancholic superfluities, that come in more than one member of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often occurs in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it behoves you to administer to him once purging of col, and then the salve of basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is done in .ij. manners: one is with the cup, and drawing forth the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the vein, and draw it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The hip is treated this way: first, raise the leg with very hot water, until the large muscle becomes tender,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then pull the leg of the patient from above the hip to just below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut open the vein in one place, or in two, or in three, of a wide size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then let the black blood flow out and draw it with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much muscle is exposed as the virtue of the patient can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then the wound, and he commands that he lay upon it black pitch-infused meat;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And recommence evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of the leg is according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and raise the leg of warm water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bain, then heat it at the fire, and then place it on the vein long from the head to the knee, or in the part below to the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the leather to the incision, and scarify the vein on each side, until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is seen red and black, and when it enters or the leather seems as if a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then bring the point below, until it is lifted from the leather, and then put it lightly on the incision.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then place the knife in another location above three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then lift it to the root, as you have done before, and place it on another incision, as you did at first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then make another cut, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut to the bottom of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then trace and lift until the second incision; then extract it incision by incision, until it is all out, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and raise it, then put a needle to all that is one.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and the thread and pull it out, and put under that one right, and turn your hand from one side and the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep that it does not break, because if it breaks, then one cannot draw it out nor raise it, and it comes to annoyance for the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it all out, then put over the place of the wound wool moistened in wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the bone is compressed and crooked and enveloped all together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if it is necessary that you split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cover the bone is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cover the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a large curve, for if it were fine, it would cover the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where no herbs nor trees grow, and in land that has no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in the legs, and this occurs due to rotting that comes under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes from within the body of serpents and worms, lodged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the color changes, and the vein begins to rise out, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder opens up, it is necessary that you envelop it with a piece of plank from one and a half to two fingers wide, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the plank on the leg, and every time that it hurts on the outside, then wrap around the plank, and the knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut it at its root, until it is fully grown out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, and bring forth abscess and rot there, and a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore for this reason it should be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein when it is treated is 5 palms long, or 10.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And one man came to me, from whom it had issued out of 10 palms in length, and when you cut it, it put out 1 ray or pit, and it pierced until the bottom
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So that all in issue; and let be emptied the matter that is within, and administer to the place medicines preventing putrefaction any day, then the cure like the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And no time at this vein main reins, and same when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And there comes much of pits, and from which it jumps reins; cure then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land “ox disease,” because it often happens to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body moving up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it well by the way it travels from limb to limb, as long as it reaches the skin where it goes, and then leaps further;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by rot of some humors, like those that come from serpents and worms and parasites in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And one doubts its malignancy, because when it travels through the body and goes up to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps entering, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drained, if one can only flee when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so therefore it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong ligament tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and treat the wound, and if it is drawn too far into the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it inflames the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, hold under it the eyebrow form, then cut above, and the wound treat;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body with medicinals soluble for the bad humors corrupted.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if worse from meats engendering putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This sickness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and after that, I saw it rise as if a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	More quickly than anything else, as if living silver when it departs from its place.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that place and settles in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little while after it spreads throughout the whole body, until it arrives in the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it returned again throughout her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never before seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many who well had moved pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it like this, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and veins uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, that constraint appears.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious and who have moist bodies and veins returned.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if it lies above and below evenly, and then cut upon it as much as that constraint appears to be in its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure of those who discharge wind, such as foul pills, and pills of serpentine, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small ones, and hairy, and joined.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some that have two angles, and those that have tongues, and some that have parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and some that fall in any member, if it falls in two ways: either in the principal member
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	...such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you after, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then it is necessary that you take care in the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many situations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not entirely embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is on top of the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is when there is scotomy and sode and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps it is without power from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wound moisture white seeming to poultices, and leaps also like burning charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears to you, then hold off from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near to the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the seventh moves also like the pulse, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	So then knowing without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not have a vein is that without any foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and gasps loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the small ribs; and gets great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested flesh leaps from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and nothing of straw comes out through the intestine route, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine comes out mixed with blood, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and auxiliary and spine of the back and groin and hips and legs, and the seeming member, are safe according to more arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for this reason that you do the same thing.
