Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man with an arrow shot or falling into the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and withdrew it from another side under the fat of the ear, and was healed without any sense or pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And treat with a game an arrow which fell into the fat of the eye below the paper down.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was returned, and one could only reach its point toward the shaft
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large of a Turkish bow, to all one and a half lighter without ears; the game was healthy, and nothing bad happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And treat an arrow of the throat to a Christian, and it was the Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was the bristles, and I subtly traced until I betrayed it, and were healed the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And betrayed an arrow to one man, who it was in his stomach or belly, and thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that after thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and I removed it, and betrayed it further, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose arrow fell or struck on his back, and the wound was sewed up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds inconvenience in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sewed up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remains so suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And treat an arrow in a man of princes the king, who it was stuck in his thigh.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was a little declining on the right side; and the arrow was completely drawn back
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after three days had passed. So I found the wound very narrow
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it to be a very fine tent, and did not feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt a prickling and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on its place a plaster atrifical and digestive, because the wound did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared to me the holes of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put the plaster on his hand that day, and stitched up the wound straight, and the patient remained so for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow i.e., one day inside his flesh; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound medicine agu corrosive by hand that day, until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and the feel, and feel the head of the arrow which is becoming set in its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it pierced well the ends about four months;
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I widened the wound so much that I put pliers on it, and mine on one side and the other, and it could not slip out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore do not cease to be subtle and devise ways of instruments, until I took one day pliers well made
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I worked on it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirrors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was soldered together, and the patient was healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	So that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot comprehend everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare very well to a small thing, and to those that are present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are not found in members where they are fixed except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or from another place;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which has gone further than where it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and it has never come out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it has not yet come out, leave it as long as the flesh is rotten around it, and let the opening be clean.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is set in bone, and it cannot move, then leave it so for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and therefore if it leaps, and if it does not leap, then pierce around it, that is to say forest subtly, until the ligaments around are spread, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is set in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not treat it, but leave it so until it is equal after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes to this place, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not come to this place,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without ill effects, then let the healing process take place.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be pulled out easily, then administer poultices as I have told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body and it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the entire tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then treat it with no suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if you cannot because of the constriction of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nor nerve, nor vein, then make an opening as large as the wound;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the arrowhead by which it is held,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you loosen the bone that is enfolded into two parts at its center as much as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can extract it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and do it subtly so that you don't break the arrow, but rather extract it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then lay it until its surroundings are softened, then treat it, because extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood goes against you, then administer what we have said of the treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard yourself from the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put everything as you can to remove the arrow safely,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow struck him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest help that there can be, and if you cannot do it, put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where one sees or feels nothing in it, or the skin is swollen.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then upwards, as long as the tongs can take it, and then extract it; if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is stuck in it, pull out the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft has fallen and you see to administer binding, then administer one tool of hair;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the tool; and then pull out;
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is lodged, one puts i. instrument with a pointed end into it, to help in the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is encircled, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then cure the wound as is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the hip or abdomen or bladder or ribs and it is nearby, and you can cut into it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And guard yourself from cutting the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then sew up the wound if it is necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of an eye, and look here at the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many varieties: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the butting head is also like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To butt at the tip of the arrow, as this is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for butting and for knowing is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins from which one is healed there are thirty-one, of which it has or head sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say: two veins that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbesch";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are on the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly draws blood are five in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it is on the inner side of the arm, and the common people call it "the vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "fascia" and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic vein,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the common people call it "the vein of the heart"; And the basilic one is on the outer side
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is on the fossa
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one that we open which is manifestly apparent on the pouch
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the sap vein is the vein which is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two veins;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot is there are three veins: one of these is below the curve of the pouch of the left costal
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right leg; and the vein that is called "ness", which is in the ankle of the other leg.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein of the veins that are behind the ears if it helps with old catarrs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the saining, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two lengths depending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	and where you feel the pulse below your shoulder, grasp it;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all the way up the vein
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cover and the skin and the vein well two points to traverse, and make blood flow as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain and tie it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for ancient migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and suddenly, and inflammation accustomed, and to the body of the tears sharp to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of blood are such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulsation below his throat, and then  becomes filled with blood.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lightly raise the heart above the vein toward your index finger, and thrust the lance below.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	And lift the vein upward, and the cup, just as you have done in two other veins, and draw out blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and place your hand over the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about this and their cuping and their extraction, as the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting of the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting of the cephalic for ancient face diseases, and for migraine, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting it, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "flogger," whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold firm with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never open it with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper for the flames to be too large; and to heal across, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in two tear ducts helps the eyes, and the nose, and the cheek, and to the orbicularis oculi muscle, and to diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healing are that the patient straightens his neck by twisting with a band, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the healthy one, and let it be healthy through the length, a bit of the long of the flame a bit wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make a correction of blood, as much as you need it, and then tie up cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein opening of the neck is good for fever, and for sore throat, and for diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient tightens his neck, then pulls his nose with his left hand
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and takes a subtle long flame, and places it between the two nostrils in the space.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well until now, and the blood will begin to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it flow too much, and make it flow blood according to your need, then bind it for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The sap of the two-fingered vine helps in the treatment of the alaine, and at the beginning of measles, and in many diseases, and in emphysema, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and estiomenes.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the sap are that the patient strains his neck under both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then cleanse the vein with a long point broadly, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then redo the other part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and restrain both veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, that the wound be cleansed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of cleansing the limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps in collecting in the mouth, and in the corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and sores and ulcers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you know them by this that they are black, and by this that around them there are veins small black ones:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore, one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are doubtful.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If one takes the largest of each side, and also make two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein beneath the tongue helps after the cephalic vein, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the veins are that the patient should lie between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks down on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then feel one and the other, and do not go too deep into them, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm which are commonly bled from are felt in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking at one or all  a single, fine vein like an olive, subtle as it is, as you say, and it is called "the ansel";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very well-known, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening veins that are flat with large visible blood, and which contain large and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where it has subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments that are under the throat, and on the neck, and on the chest, and on the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely, and that he be wary of the artery which is under.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flowing of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not at all be pricking flame, but cutting as a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not clearly open, then it is necessary that you restrain it, and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no vein of it, or you  sane in its place the vein within the arm: it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cautery to the knife as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary so that you extract the arm, that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a sharp knife.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, because it is of the artery; therefore avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise up high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your leg on a long length [of something], then remove your leg if it is without stiffness, which many times happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	bind his arm and leave it so, and do not move it the patient; and be on guard, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the limb is not stiff and it pains him, and the medicine is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and stiffen the limb.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark of pistachio, and make it into a paste, and take one of the halves and bind it well up until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding stops, it is well; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of bleeding is not always achieved in all positions for the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein's blood flow in the middle helps that it treats blood from the head above and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the healer that he feel for the nerve which is below, and if they are pricked too much, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the wounds become sore, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any men for its subtlety, then it is necessary that you cleanse it with the instrument of healing; and withdraw the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, then make a cut along it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting of the head helps, that it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is proper to bleed by pricking at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, for this is the safest of all the veins, because it does not have any nerves nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is proper to seek the lightest spot, and it harms nothing if one fails the first time, and one begins again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance swells the veins in some men, when one fails the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bloodletting, is that it is administered only for the sake of health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are or cut: namely cephalic, femoral, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of Lent on Monday, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must bleed on the first day or the third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting that is administered to the sick has no set hour, but when there is need, it is done every day or night, at all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one should not bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying child from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not let them bleed those who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the bowels with a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If he has much phlegm retained so that the veins do not draw out the superfluous impurities harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Do not bleed those who are too full of meat, nor those who are drunk, until they have sobered up, nor the dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if it is worse after colic passion, and vomiting, and stomach upset, and multiplication of labor in women, and childbirth, vigil, and fasting, and that which all virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly bring them to balance, if it is thick, through meats and drinks and medications, if you have the power for it.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtly thin the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and drain the vein of the lower arm at the third part as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself on that day of labor, and of thrusting, and of lust, and of similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be tied and joined, and let the healthy hand be higher than the one that is treated, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then loosen the bandage in the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct itself;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with your hands, until the veins swell and are felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the veins with a drop of old oil, then place his finger of his left hand upon that vein below its place an inch where he wants to bleed.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein may not be broken and made worse by the iron.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which are as thick as cords when bleeding, and some that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the cautery upon it, it retracts from the cautery, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, if the wound is too tight, for this reason it is necessary that the healers be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, it begins again a little below where it was previously, as long as the lesion is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the lesion is inflamed and the patient fears, let him leave it for one or two days, and not tie up his arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	For by chance an abscess may come; do not let him bathe then, afterwards begin the bloodletting if he wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small, or the vein is too fine and you doubt that it isn't as much blood as you see, so apply fire to that same opening straight into the flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And work a little gently, so that the eyes are inflamed; because this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place inflamed, then do not begin the bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil on top, because it calms the body's blood and is good in this place the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the oil to every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and the same thing happens to the same bone when it is put back in place; so subtly the sinew and departs when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens often, even when it is not drained except for the time when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and put on top a sponge moistened in water and some hot oil, and restrain it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the bloodletting from the vein, and if it remains in place after a few days without any blackness or greenish color, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see it, put on no thing of aloe or frankincense made into juice of calamint, mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance appear at the shrine of the basilica: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore shun that you put on anything of those we have said, for by chance it may be without the artery; but make one plaster dry to harden the place, then heal with another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it ooze until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it befits him who is pale and weak, and needs the extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it befits him to bleed less and often, and he should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is safe from a decrease in blood and damage to the nerves, and is better than bleeding from a long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to the one whose body requires the bloodletting, it is fitting to give moistened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is dried out, treat him with blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, moisten the bread before bloodletting with syrup of quince, or with syrup of honey aromatic with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints at bloodletting, after the issuing of some blood, it is fitting that he imbibe broth of meat and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the opening of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to drain his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong flesh, he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another place, they must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood in his body which is already exhausted, and brings on fever; so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening as far as it will go into patches.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	since you cure all the conditions of health, and put your hand on his arm when it is healthy, that death may not come in place of pain
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not fitting when you see the arm dislocated, and draw blood a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	and if it is curved, let him extend his arm fully, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it stay until it heals the second time; or if you prick it with the tip of the flame, until the skin which is frozen from the vein is gone.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on top i. point of oil returned to a liquid and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood the second time, let it be drained in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein to draw blood from the arm is located in the place of the vein at the head for that reason she is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of drawing blood from it is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then draw blood now through it, neither from the wide nor the long side.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and draw blood well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot flow out, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood in the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not reapply the hand in hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	bind the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it is cut across, and if you cut it through completely, it does no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not cut too deeply into it, because the nerves are underneath all the flesh exposed.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, if it has become numb within the wound, and cannot be moved.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then place oil and wool on top of the vein to soothe it, and do this for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of the left hand is as good for the disease of mice, and do everything just as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The vein of the saphenous is as good for all the illnesses that are below the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	just as diseases of the groin, and retention of flowers, and illness of the hips, and thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of this vein are that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it bleeds
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	so then one should select the largest vein or at the ankle, which he thinks best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you drain it above the foot, guard yourself from the nerves that are below, and drain it transversely as well when cutting; and let the flame be annealed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot insert it, put the foot back in water, and allow the vein to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the needle is needed the first time, start again the second from above a bit, because the vein is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do the same with the soft tissue of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of fire, and its puncture is worth to the pain of the hip when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its puncture are that the patient lies down in the bath and is pulled upwards from the ankle 4 fingers' width while twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in every way that you can, and across
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cauterize it, because the flesh is dry, and it is much restored by men's hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then heal any vein that opens or below the foot, and towards the small thigh, and guard the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do as much cauterization of blood as you see fit, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and restrain it; now she is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of the sucking blisters
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Sucking blisters are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction which is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is with heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And suction that is done by piercing and drawing blood is done in fourteen places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely in the sum of the head; and the other is within the neck
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in two ribs of the neck; and the windpipe below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the windpipe from the two shoulders; and the windpipe above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the windpipes within the two arms; and the windpipes of the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the leeches on the two ankles; and suction treatment does not deal with blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because of this it does not weaken one as much, as is done with bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither on a hot nor cold fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it must be suctioned, or for customs, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and midway and at every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to vomit, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and those who suffer from fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who suffer from a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see through blood and bruises and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is emitted from the month, we command to ventilate after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the muse helps to the grievance of the head... which comes to the eyes, and it does not suit that this be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not suit those who are of a cold complexion to use it, or who have phlegm, because it causes them great discomfort.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it is not proper that the elderly use it, nor those who have or cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal with this, often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction applied on the neck is in the place of the vein from the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is worth it for the treatment of the pleura.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to the opening of the channel of the peritoneum, and everything, and to the repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and there it is necessary to not push too hard, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause obstruction in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The venting of the two ribs in the neck is good for pains in the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the healer that he express his hand when putting it in, so that he doesn't cut the artery and there comes a discharge of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The venting under the chin is good for mouth ailments, and gum rot, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the groins is as good as three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the patient not to pierce them too much, because they are bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the base, and for diseases of below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and be of iron, that she has need to well suck; and perhaps, if she were thin, she would break; and in this I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are helpful, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the knees, and of the bladder, and relax the flowers; and are in their place at the .ij. shins, and the .ij. ankles, and all the same they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in more dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and suck temperately, and put it steadily, and move equally, and do not cease doing this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then finish, and put back the suction cups, and take ward in the disposition of the body, because there are such who have tanned flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, then it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to gently open the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, then it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, then we only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want much blood, then we start again often; and if the vein is thick, then we prick it deeply, and the end is that the hairs are pierced suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for someone who has thick and hard skin, and who have many pores, that you oil their places with cupping jars of an appetizing and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is inflamed, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucumber seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is weeping, of cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one who is being treated has tender skin and large pores, then it should not be put on oil at all;
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the aeration of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or china water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, rises from ease with myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or buckthorn water, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to suck blood before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after suction.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he lie down when he ought to sneeze and when he is sneezing.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And ward off those who are jaundiced when they are ill and if their skin is too dry and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then it is necessary that he eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce at the meal, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and to drink juices of cucumber and  beef broth and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and quince, and quinces and small eels and sparrows;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will be weaned, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no man at any time triacle or musk before or after the weaning, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the wine be subtle, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cupping glasses that are put on without hurting are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the groin and the hips and the hip, because those members do not suffer to be hurt on their skin.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the breasts when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and groin to lessen the swelling of the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or displaces the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it is done when he is placed upon the liver and on the mouse when there is retained windiness.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of boiled water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in diseases of the lungs, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water only, or with water in which herbs suitable to this have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have two boards of wide breadth and half a palm in length, and have on the side toward the middle one small hole, as for putting in a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of iron, soft before so that it does not pierce the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And have in the middle a crossbar of iron or steel, to put a candle set.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are other than those of the old, and of the thin ones than of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one thus place this suction cup upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	embrace the candle of wax or one linen cloth, and put it within the suction cup on the side that is inside the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and those should be on the opening we have said, so that when one wishes, there goes the vapor, and remove the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take up the lining as before, and begin it often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, in all sharpness, has no rod nor opening, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only so much;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suckings are administered only to members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their denuded flesh, such as two or three, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the qualities of the user are that when you find suckings which are in clear sweet waters without bitterness, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a nut of sweet water until they become familiar and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let it be cleansed with a lancet and a suction cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on herbs.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and have fallen, if it is the place where a suction cup can be put, then put one, because it helps a lot after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place carefully and then with water, very well, and then press it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place heals too much after the herbs, then soak one cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on, until the swelling is reduced;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wound is multiplied, put on it pounded vitriol, or alum, and similar things, until it is stretched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you put on the wound half of peeled beans, and let them stay until they dry on the wound, so it will now stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other beans.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the beans will not be taken, rub the wound with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the pus comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them up, and as soon as they feel the blood, they become inflamed;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are oozing, sprinkle on a bit of alum and soot powdered, or ashes, then they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoring of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear child, that the matters of this chapter are not found in any of the ancient books, nor has anyone ever read them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the knowledge is kept secret in our land, because I have never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except by the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have mastered the science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
