Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It behooves us therefore to say or prologue of this book the sum of the word and chapters where the sages put his understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick person on one side and the other, if any thing does not them quickly, as weakness of body, or child, or old man.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the pain is not very strong, or too cold; and avoid cold things, that is to say, cold meats, and meat of lamb and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill himself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or expansion of matter in the limb; then return the sick person to his first government that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and pies, and belly of beef, and eels, and fresh fish, and red wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment they regain strength and the fracture heals faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decrepit do not heal well nor join together according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but if there is no cure, reset the broken bone, that is, large tendons which are held and join the limb together, until it forces as it was before; and to that point of its work, and for this reason, it is necessary to nourish him with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the side and another that goes to a point, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with fracture, and fracture to a small crack entirely.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each manner it has its engine, and its instrument proper in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And is known the fracture of the bone by those that its end is twisted, and opens well outwards, and feels in pressing with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting nor feeling at touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have torsion, or fracture, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you should not move it by hand, but put on the remedies that come after here, and then restrain it carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which goes in the arc, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary now to put them together equally, so that abscesses do not come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses come there, then let it alone until the abscesses are calmed for no day;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then set it straight to the joint as you can lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restorations of those where there are pieces; then restrain, as it befits afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone it has broken pieces, two parts, whether it is hands or feet, or to your hand if it's small limbs, or two cords, or one cord and to your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken limb are exposed, you skillfully move all the additions into their places as much as you can, and keep that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if it is arranged nicely, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come by their work abscess hot and contraction to the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, so warn the patient well that he does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And watch well that the limb is so assured that he feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then it is not in place, and it behooves to put it in such a disposition that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and guard that it be placed straightly, that twisting come not when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are little limbs, such as arms and legs and similar things: so it is fitting to envelop them with cloths of soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those who are thick, such as the thigh and leg: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard linen, because the wide linen embraces the whole large limb, and restrains it from all parts equally, so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around light splints, three or four tours according to the limb, and restrain your hand a little on all the linen, then go above the fracture and restrain less, than the fracture and then push away the fracture a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen little by little, until you reach a large part of the healthy place, then take another linen, and turn around directly above the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and restrain it moderately, neither too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first place above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the bandages of linen or cloth, until it is all equal, then bind everything above.i. with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put something soothing for the abscess on top that removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then restrain with your splints, and be of half a width of a broad cane properly cut, or of wood from which one makes the cleats, or of palm branches, and be according to this figure;
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint placed on a fracture be a little larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as is necessary for the limb of small or large size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then fasten on the splints also as you did in the first hour, then tie them above with a thread evenly, just as in the first hour on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more tight is it above, less below; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in works of fools who make their cords from linen twisted too finely, and this is a great error, for the thread cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not be that between each star there be less than two fingers' width of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is irritated by the edges of the stars after the tightening in their healthy places, then put under them pads of linen or wool felt so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a break and the tendons are broken, I will say about its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to set all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is great, it is not fitting to put on splints before after five days or seven, or more according to your certainty of a boil coming about hot.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour that stands at the walls of the mill, and confide it with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, neither too light nor too thick, and in use, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in more dispositions, and even to women and to small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  three pieces of ginger, laudanum, nutmeg, asafoetida, and Arabic gum and myrrh and aloes, each  five; alechil eight, and make it into powder, and mix it with a good amount of egg. If the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to more men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, ana .x.  z.; myrrh and aloes, ana .viiij. z.; acaice vi. z.; Armenian bollic .x. z., and grind well, and confit with water or the white of an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of ointment for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and it soothes the pain that occurs, and the use of the bone, and the bruise: take new wool, and moisten it in lard and oil cooked, and put it on its place. This plaster does not restore anything, but it is good to soothe a hot abscess, and remove properly pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of ointment which restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and earth laurel leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of ointment for the restoration of bone fracture and to lessen the remainder of the abscess. Take root of vismalve, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of quince, each one part; and grind, and confit with wine, and if the limb is scabby, confit it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of ointment more forceful than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of vismalve, and flax seed, balm, melilot, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Galen says in his book that one should put on the broken limb for restoration only a certain thing made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and that it should be between two soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that one must put upon the broken limb, to restore, things dry a little warm, like myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of making an ointment that is good for the injury and pain: take mugwort and chicory of men chopped, or feathers of bird, and wormwood, and equal parts, and grind them, and make it into an ointment and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not loosen it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, no rest, or swelling, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the ointment now; and take light cloth, and sponge of sea moistened, and dip in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest an hour, then put upon it dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it on with a bandage, until you are sure of the heat of the abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the member rest, and be removed the pain, then begin again the fine dressing, and a little plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before; and make it subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed and red and pain and swelling are entirely gone, and you have need of plaster and linen, then begin again as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing comes to the member of what we have said, then do not unbind it except after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and no time leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the breakage heals and approaches the alignment of the flesh above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	therefore he restrains more than before, and strengthens his flesh, as I have said before; and if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that no nourishment can come there;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	therefore apply hot water to it, every time you loosen it, and slightly remove the cloth each day;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	for by this work the nourishment to the limb is cut off, and it mends slowly those that do foolish things, who leave the limb twisted; it is bad, and so is this work dangerous, and I see nothing else than to leave it and work it straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures are, and diverse shapes, and the causes are destined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made by the thrust of a sword, and the collarbone all the bone until it's surface which is below the bone, as it is done with hay or staff; and for this reason, this kind of fracture is called "haywire".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and is the wound of these two fractures large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or splitting or of the collarbone of stone, or of the cheek on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating, which approaches to the skin that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is set back in the bone as subtle as a thread, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is made either by a stone striking, or by falling, or by something similar, and drives the piece of bone inward, and it is in the place like how blacksmiths do when they forge on the cauldrons; so enters the piece of stone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have or whose heads are moist bones, like children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and there are all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are torn away from them like stars; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by the retraction on them, and the examination of tendons, and by the corrupted cartilage that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of capillary blood is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs on it, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, take heed of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and eyes staring and reddening, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an escapable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it behooves you to remove the bone before the fourteenth day, as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone may not rot and bring about the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes as far as the membrane that covers the brain, then it behooves you to split the cracked portion thus: and take hold of the head of the injured patient gently, and expose as much as you can of the bone and the figure of the wound more carefully than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the bleeding comes when uncovering the bone, or abscess, then help them as it is fitting, and that you fill the space with soft cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and be sure of no more bleeding; then begin to carefully remove the bone, and this is done according to .ij. ways of work: one way is that you cut in a narrow section before, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make one other incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of incisions of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron, and in working lightly, so that you do not cut the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and out, then it behooves you to pierce it through, so that you administer splints with drill bits, not more than that lest they pierce beyond the bone of the test, and must have above the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point beyond the bone; and you should have several more, so that each comes in its place to the width of the bone, so that you have drill bits for all tests; and this is the form of the three kinds of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the broken bone are that you put one drill bit on the bone and turn with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the drill bit elsewhere a little after, and so do all around, then cut with the cutting instruments the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like tweezers, pliers; and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you will have the bone pierced and treated, then it behooves you to remove the piece of bone which is remaining from the bone with any instrument similar to a cutting tool, but it behooves that it is more durable and subtler than the other cutting tool;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it remains nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, then the bones are lightly moved with i.e. instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is drier; and he praises it much, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears open, so that when you have uncovered that part, then you place beneath the head of this lens-shaped incision tool, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not dig in one part, and it is the part sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is toward the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and be well guarded of the cloth that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, then the bone should be gently lifted, for it is well raised without pain, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that asperity and remove the scales with a fine razor, of which you must have various quantities, in order to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with large razors, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not cease until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer the cause according to its placement; and this thing is not returned to him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, it is necessary that you take one piece of linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so that you do not injure the wound, then administer above one other linen, and do not restrain it more than just as much as it holds the wound only;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let it remain so for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of vetiver, and powder of incense, and arnica, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer further medicines mild without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and guard that the wound be well clean, that you do not leave there any ointment, nor do you leave there any assembling of flesh, for when flesh assembles upon the brain's covering, it corrupts and becomes sore, and happens to the patient great malice; for when one puts upon the soft thing biting, it stings upward.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take ward then, if any bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, so is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackening does not come there except for the medicine that we have put upon it, that its virtue has, then it behooves you to take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and glue one drape, and put it upon the soft thing;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure of ways of cures that it is necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that no times are broken the two parts of the two above, or one by the alone, because they are two bones; and this below is cartilaginous, and does not break at all, if not forced to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you place your little finger or between the two bones, and put each fracture inside with your index finger, and to the pouch outwardly, as long as the bone returns according to its natural form;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and it cannot come to its place, then you must put it even at the head of a stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another splint, and hasten to restore it the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if this is not possible, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed, then bind to the head of the knee ten thicknesses of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the thicknesses be so thick that they fill the hollows of the knee.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And said any restorer that one must moisten the tents in butter, and change each day. It does not seem to me well, but it is proper that they be moistened in the confection of egg yolk and powder of mill; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts in their place goose feathers instead of tents, and so with i.e. one sheet of cloth wrapped around it, and holds the bandage, and breathes the patient amongst; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess comes to the new ones while you are working on it, if you put cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in one poke of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess comes, put a plaster from outside, of sesame flour, and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then put light dressings on top, and do not tie them too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then remove it with suitable instruments, then stitch up the wound, and cure it with things that help to heal flesh and bones, and plasters and ointments that are suitable for it.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the bone, then treat it with bandages, and put in pieces of cloth, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is outside only so much, and is not broken in two, except that it buckles inward, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the sick person; and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then put your index finger of the right hand, and push the fracture inward lightly, and fix it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is separated in two, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a rupture, so restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jawbone cerote, and put on i drapel double; and put on the drapel a great estele well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it up as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, so untie it on the third day, and then reset what is changed; and put a plaster on top, of powdered mill with an abundance of egg or sesame flour, after which you have removed the cerote; and put on top of the plaster light linen, and if the plasters dry up, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it is healed in 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, so administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward no piece of bone has been removed; so subtly of the bone with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, so close the wound, if it is wide, and put upon it one plaster suitable for this, to hinder flesh, until it be healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is like this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which is the broken bone; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put each of the fractures to your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor blemish.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it more, so put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or wool, and be thick according to your need; and gently lift the bone, and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you put each of the fractures as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder back with force because it comes in front, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his side, and put under the shoulder one hour glass, and push the minister's shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder be lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two sides, and if you find it fractured, then it is necessary that you split above; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any mounting, then cut at one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, in order to guard against displacement:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it seems like a spoon, and is not at all curved, and be as wide as it is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and have two heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the break of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of the abscess hot, then cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, then apply the wound with dressings and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten one cloth in rose oil and honey and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of a bone when it is without wounds and without cutting is that you place on the bone a plaster of milled powder and egg yolk, and put light dressings on top, and put a spear under the seat, if you need it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a very wide bandage of one palm in width, then put one double cloth on top of the dressings and plaster; then take a thin board three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandaged area, so that the ends of the bandage hang down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage on the neck, and lower the healthy shoulder, and lower the broken shoulder; and reset each part, and when you see that the splint holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the broken bone, then reward them every day, and when the ligaments relax, then restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps i. small pillow under the shoulder, to raise the arm up; so it will relieve the fracture of the shoulder by aligning the shoulder, or you bind his arm to the neck, and do not unbind it unless an ill accident comes, until xx days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then recommence the splint, if you see that he needs it, and restrain it and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most at xxviii days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder breaks or its place is loosened, and it is not known by any force; if the apparatus is placed according to the figure of the break, and it is reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on .i. double drape; then put on a broad and subtle splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is uneven in any part of the shoulder, so apply those uneven parts with linen bandages, so that the splint lies evenly; and then restrain it with a very strong bandage tightly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the bond every day; and every time that it softens, so restrain it, and put back the splint if it is outside its place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in .xx. days or in xxv, And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, because it is not bone that easily moves out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone has gone forward and is not below the heart, then do as follows, and apply the bone, and do what we have said in the break of the collarbone to soothe an abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the outside. And when it is broken in the middle, it declines toward the toes, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of support, and thirst, and perhaps vomits blood, and the bones are well exposed in the broken bone, and it smells foul.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the sides of the two bones with your hands, and skillfully brings them together in all ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put plaster and bandages above the fine layer of salt, or some other light paste, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the band around the back, and restrain it firmly, and reward every hour the bandage, and if it loosens, tighten it; and if it needs to be untied, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hasten then, and untie it, and remove what has come from the bandages, and address those things in ways of healing; then reapply the bandage, and restrain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the head within, and they bend only for that reason because they are glassy; and one feels it well upon inquiry on the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you place equal the fracture, as it should be. And then put the plaster, and restrain it with a splint, if you need it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is leaning inward, the patient feels very great pain and pricking, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and also pains, and coughs and vomits great plants of blood, and this is of grave health, and the ancients have placed great engines upon it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to bring the rupture to the outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that some put suction cups on the spot to suck out  fluids, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cup pulls out superfluities to the spot for the arrangement of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say of you it must cover the place with wool dipped in hot oil, and put a tent between the ribs to make the flesh equal, then be cured from the cure of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone which pricks the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it behooves to split on the place of the broken rib, and it behoove to put under .i. instrument to ward off the syfac; and henceforth one must trench the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew the .ij. lips of the wound, if it is great, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed. And if abscesses comes, so put on cloth moistened in rose oil, and put on the place; and cure while the place of that which it behoove abscess, and be lying softly on the side where it should, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take heed if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that he is mortal in many cases, and if he moves them and feels well when they are pulled and poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one takes care of him.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take heed if his legs are softened, and if the accident is in his hands, and on his back there is windiness and ejection without volition; and when one has him lying on his belly, there is ejection without volition. And when he is lying on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. Know that he is mortal: if he does not labor well in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, so put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and tie it with a band, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with one suture, then cure it with ointment inhibiting flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," then put your fist from your left hand into it, and set it equal to the other hand in your power, then put on the plaster and splint on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are bones dislocated, do this, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes it happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, it has not happened from a little weakening at the top; and making long, and declining to the side, and comes to the patient pain in the place, and tingling, and swells what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as much as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the figure of it; and if the fracture is at the top only, put equal to this fracture, as long as it is in a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines to the inside, put the patient on his belly, as long as the restoration of this fracture becomes apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you would have it even, put it upon the splint, then put upon a strip of wood or of bark, and restrain the splint so that it does not move; and apply the place under the ribs, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep upon his healthy side or upon his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes to it, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and put upon it what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as it is fitting, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take one stick of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads of two ropes together, and lift them up, and place the patient on one seat; then place his broken arm on top of the stick, as far as it comes to the armpit, and make a curvature in the stick, then put on any heavy thing or minister's extend it down; then put the patient's fracture equal to his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his stretcher and ties his hand to his neck, then instructs two ministers that one holds what is above the fracture in his hands, and the other holds below by about a foot, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more forth, restrain .i. the linen under the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to its part. And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put .i. linen medium under the seat, and .i. other towards the outside, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the outside, it is necessary to put .i. linen lightly, without labor, until the fracture is equal on the top, and on the side; then place equal the fracture, as it is fitting, and restrain it, if an abscess does not come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does come there, do not restrain it until .vij. days, and put on linen half in oil and rose oil, until the abscess has calmed; then restrain it, and the manner of restraining it is that you place the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the drape, and restrain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm be in its place of stars, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints, and put on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint .i. two of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the fracture .iij. two on each side; then restrain on the splints, in the same way as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the setting of the bones, and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess hot, so let it bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each three days the bandage, that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or the sores can not come to the limb for that it is too much inflamed. If it is healed, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents come, so do not unbind until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion plain of wool evenly, and look every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or the bandages are softened; if it is healed by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat as we have before set forth, in such manner that the meat be at first thin; and when he begins to regain strength, let it be coarse. And it is custom that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days altogether; and then one must unbind and administer baths and medicines of ointment for the place to heal. And if the constriction is bad and entangled, so delay unbinding for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of .ij. bones, which are called the two "fossil," because one is small, and that follows the socket; and the other is large, and that is below, towards the little toe; by chance breaks the large fossil alone, or the small, and by chance and both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fossil is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large is broken, it is the healing bad, and more grieves than when they are broken both together. If it is the small fossil that is broken alone, then it is necessary to gently extend it, and put even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large fossil, then it is necessary to restrain more strongly; and extend it on one cushion, and hold the socket of the hand higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed on him himself, and one cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers of his arm to the part below his hand, or to one linen, and some other ministers to one other above. And then put the mirrors even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any dislocated that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make it as above with the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, then glue it i.e., a bandage of cerate made from rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard nor too soft; and cover it with a bandage subtly, until the abscesses are appeased.
